FOREWORD
When the Director-General of  the National Youth 
Service Corps, Major General S Ibrahim Assoc. Prof. 
DSS FHSN MTRCN assumed duty on 10th May , 
2019, he was clear and unequivocal about his determination to 
make deep impact on the Scheme. Suffice it to say he had then 
returned to a familiar terrain, having served as top Military aide 
to two of  his predecessors. Three years down the line, keen 
watchers of  NYSC are more than convinced that his is a mission 
to turn around the fortunes of  the Scheme. His visionary , 
dynamic and dogged approaches to administration are not only 
reaping numerous impressive results, but have also been sources 
of  inspiration to all members of  Staff, Corps members and other 
admirers.  Thus, the third anniversary of  the administration 
presents yet another opportunity for the NYSC Family and 
friends of  the Scheme to reflect on his exemplary leadership and 
celebrate his numerous achievements.
As is the tradition of  the Scheme, the last three years have 
witnessed numerous in-house and public functions, which are in 
pursuit of  its mandate. Expectedly , such events would feature

The publication will be of  immense benefit to NYSC Staff,

including researchers, as it will further enrich their grasp of  
policies and programmes of  the Scheme.

PREFACE
The National Y outh Service Corps was established by 
Decree No. 24 of  22nd May , 1973 by the then General 
Yakubu Gowon regime in furtherance of  the Federal 
Government's post-war policy of  Reconstruction, Reconciliation 
and Rehabilitation. The aim was to raise a crop of  disciplined, 
detribalized and patriotic youths that would be posted to serve in 
communities/locations other than theirs, and seek permanent 
employment outside their states of  origin thereby fostering the 
much desired national unity and integration. To further set the 
Scheme on the path of  goal attainment and dynamism, Decree 
No. 24 of  1973 was repealed and replaced with Decree No. 51 of  
16th June, 1993 which is now NYSC Act CAP N84 Laws of  the 
Federation of  Nigeria 2004. 
The objectives of  the Scheme as contained in the Enabling Act 
are to inculcate discipline in Nigerian youths by instilling in them 
 v

The foregoing objectives are pursued through the four Cardinal 
Programmes of  the Scheme: Orientation Course, Primary 
Assignment, Community Development Service and Winding-
up/Passing-out Programme. 
a tradition of  industry at work and of  patriotic and loyal service to 
Nigeria in any situation they may find themselves; to raise the 
moral tone of  the Nigerian youths by giving them the opportunity 
to learn about higher ideals of  national achievements, social and 
cultural improvement; to develop in Nigerian youths the attitudes 
of  mind, acquired through shared experience and suitable 
training, which will make them more amenable to mobilization in 
the national interest; to enable Nigerian youths acquire the spirit 
of  self-reliance by encouraging them to develop skills for self-
employment;  to contribute to the accelerated growth of  the 
national   economy; to develop common ties among the Nigerian 
youths and promote national unity and integration; to remove 
prejudices, eliminate ignorance and confirm at first hand the 
many similarities among Nigerians of  all ethnic groups; and to 
develop a sense of  corporate existence and common destiny of  
the people of  Nigeria.
The Orientation Course introduces Corps members to the 
Scheme and prepares them for the one-year National Service. 
During the three-week programme, they are exposed to 
paramilitary drills, citizenship and leadership lectures as well as 
entrepreneurship development training, amongst others. The 
 vi
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
The second Cardinal Programme, which is Primary Assignment, 
spans through a period of  eleven (11) months. For this, Corps 
members are posted to public and private organizations from 
where they gain vital first-hand experience and on the job 
training. In addition, they are exposed to the virtues of  hard work, 
diligence and obedience to constituted authorities.
The Scheme also promotes unity , spirit of  healthy competition 
and self-development amongst Corps members through the 
assemblage of  Corps members of  diverse ethnic, religious, social, 
cultural and economic backgrounds in the Orientation Camps is 
also deliberately intended to promote the much desired national 
unity and integration. 
Running concurrently with Primary Assignment is the 
Community Development Service (CDS). This third Cardinal 
Programme is a platform for Corps members to initiate and 
execute projects aimed at improving the living standards of  their 
host communities. From inception of  the Scheme to date, 
successive batches of  Corps members have used this platform to 
add value to the society through construction of  culverts and 
bridges, tree planting, development of  farms, art-works, 
landscaping, beautification, and campaign against HIV/AIDS. 
Other notable CDS programmes are the Health Initiative for 
Rural Dwellers (HIRD), Mass Literacy Campaign, and Advocacy 
on the Sustainable Development Goals. 
vii

Winding-Up/Passing-Out Programme is the last phase of  the 
National Service during which Corps members are reassembled 
to share experiences and reappraise the service year with a view to 
making informed suggestions for the enhancement of  the 
Scheme's operations. At the end of  this exercise, Corps members, 
who meet the set requirements, are issued with the Certificate of  
National Service.
In its nearly five decades of  existence, NYSC has continued to 
make invaluable contributions to the socio-economic 
development of  the country , through the implementation of  the 
Cardinal Programmes. Apart from its leading role in the 
promotion of  unity and integration, the profound impacts of  the 
Scheme in the areas of  education, healthcare, agriculture, 
infrastructural development amongst others, have made it a 
household name in Nigeria. 
NYSC Sports and Cultural Festivals. Stakeholders in the sports 
sector and the entertainment industry are encouraged to use the 
platform to discover talented Corps members and provide them 
with career opportunities.
 
A new chapter was opened in the history of  the Scheme on 10th 
May , 2019 with Major General S Ibrahim (then a Brigadier 
General) assuming duty as its Director-General.  He is in the 
saddle after seventeen previous Chief  Executives, including Col 
AA Ali, Col SK Omojokun, Col PK Obasa, Brig Gen EA Akpan,

The Special Duties Department commemorated the first and 
second anniversaries of  his assumption of  duty with the first and 
second volumes of  this Book, which are special compilations of  
some of  his landmark speeches and achievements. As we mark the 
third anniversary of  his administration, this third volume is 
compiled as yet another reference material for members of  Staff, 
researchers and other stakeholders in the Scheme.

PROFILE OF THE NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL 
MAJ GEN S IBRAHIM ASSOC. PROF. DSS FHSN MTRCN
Major General Shuaibu Ibrahim hails from 
Nasarawa Local Government Area of  
Nasarawa State.  He attended the 
University of  Jos, where he obtained 
Bachelors and Masters Degrees in 
History (1989 and 1992 respectively) 
before proceeding to bag a Post-
Graduate Diploma in Education of  
the Tai Solarin University of  
Education, Ijebu Ode. Driven by his 
insatiable thirst for knowledge, he 
went on to obtain a PhD in History 
from the University of  Abuja in 
2007.
BACKGROUND/EDUCATION
Since his commissioning into the 
Nigerian Army , he has served in various 
capacities in Military formations across the 
country. His appointments and postings 
include:
· Institute of  Army Education 
(Research Officer). Researched and 
produced Nigerian Army Journals 
and Briefs for the Nigerian Army in 
particular and the Military in general;
MILITARY CAREER

professionalism through training and retraining of  officers, he 
attended various courses, including the Nigerian Army 
Education Corps (NAEC) Young Officers Course (1994), 
Infantry Y oung Officers Course (1996), Training Development 
Advisers Course (2004) and NAEC Officers Executive 
Management Course (5/2013).

the National Y outh Service Corps with the assumption of  duty by 
Major General Shuaibu Ibrahim (then a Brigadier General) as its 
18th Director-General. He immediately unveiled his policy thrust 
anchored on the following cardinal points:

in line with the NYSC Act for greater impact.

5. The Scheme, which marked its Forty-eighth Anniversary nd
on 22  May , 2021, has remained the most successful national 
programme established to address basic challenges that usually 
confront a developing nation and diverse society such as Nigeria, 
including issues of  national unity and integration, socio-
economic development and manpower mobility . I am proud to 
add that NYSC has distinguished itself  as the most enduring of  all 
national institutions established in the last four to five decades. 
The survival of  the Scheme is indeed a pointer to its resilience and 
continued relevance to national development. Indeed, it remains 
a worthy legacy , bequeathed to the nation by the Gowon 
administration.
6. The Scheme has continued to witness improvements in all 
spheres despite contemporary challenges, including the latest one 
occasioned by the COVID-19 pandemic. Deliberate steps have 
been taken to strengthen it for greater impact and keep alive the 
vision of  the founding fathers. The results are, indeed, 
heartwarming as seen in the invaluable contributions of  the 
Scheme to the socio-economic development of  the country , 
which have been adequately documented in these books. 
economy and a land of  bright and full opportunities for all 
citizens. It was indeed a patriotic policy thrust aimed at 
inculcating in the Nigerian youths, the spirit of  patriotism, 
discipline, self-reliance and selfless service.
7. The prospects of  the Scheme are no doubt reassuring. 
With the proposed establishment of  the National Y outh Service 
Corps Trust Fund, we look forward to having a sustainable plan 
for periodic improvement and expansion of  our Camp facilities, 
revamping of  the Skill Acquisition and Entrepreneurship 
Development programme, provision of  start-up grants for Corps

iv . Successful conduct of  Orientation Courses after 
the COVID-19 Lockdown
It would be recalled that following the outbreak of  the COVID-
19, the NYSC Management took the proactive step of  
suspending the 2020 Batch 'A' Stream 1 Orientation Course just a 
week into the exercise as a measure to avert the spread of  the virus 
to the Orientation Camps.  While the nation was still on 
lockdown, we further took the step of  presenting to the Federal 
Government, our proposal for safe and efficient resumption of  
our Orientation Course under the “New Normal” setting.   With 
the support and guidance of  the Presidential Task Force (now 
Presidential Steering Committee) on COVID-19 and the Nigeria 
Centre for Disease Control, our proposal sailed through. 
Consequently , the 2020 Batch 'B' Streams 1A, 1B, and 2 as well as 
the 2021 Batch 'A' Stream 1 and Stream 2 Orientation Courses 
were all conducted successfully . Also, the 2020 Batch 'A' Stream 1 
Corps members, whose Orientation Course was suspended in 
March 2020 as a result of  the pandemic, were recalled to Camp to 
complete their training by spreading them in convenient numbers 
to join the three streams of  the 2020 Batch 'B' Orientation 
Course. 
v . Completion of  the production of  NYSC Movie
It would be recalled that during one of  our previous interactions, I 
disclosed that the production of  an NYSC movie titled 'A Call to 
Service' was on-going. However, it was slowed down due to the 
restrictions occasioned by the COVID-19 pandemic. I am happy 
to inform you that the movie has now been completed with its 
trailers officially unveiled earlier today, and will soon be 
premiered in Cinemas across the country. It will serve 
entertainment function and also sensitize the public on the roles

Because of  our concern about the threats of  erosion in some 
Orientation Camps across the country , Management sought the 
help of  the Federal Government in tackling the problem. I am 
pleased to inform you that the Government has granted the 
request through the deployment of  the Ecological Fund to tackle 
the menace. Eight of  the Camps have been approved as 
beneficiaries in the first phase of  the intervention. While work has 
reached advanced stage in Cross River, FCT , and Taraba, it is set 
to begin in Kebbi and Nasarawa States.   
Driven by our determination to ensure that the Scheme stays in 
tune with its core mandate and the need to operate in tandem 
with global best practices, Management set up a Committee to 
chart a developmental pathway for the Scheme in the next five 
years. The development plan has already been evolved while a 
standard implementation template is being worked on.

4.       Ladies and gentlemen, I consider it appropriate to use this 
forum to acquaint you with facts on the proposal for the 
establishment of  the National Y outh Service Corps Trust Fund 
(NYSCTF). In spite of  its success story , the Scheme faces myriads 
of  challenges mainly arising from the gap in the discharge of  the 
obligations of  stakeholders. Problems such as inadequate facilities 
in Orientation Camps, lack of  or inadequate Corps Lodges, 
inadequate office accommodation for State Secretariats as well as 
Zonal and Local Government Offices of  the Scheme, amongst 
others, are faced in some States. The search for solutions to the 
aforementioned and other challenges was taken to the second 
meeting of  the NYSC Top Management with representatives of  
State Governments, Federal Capital Territory Administration 
and the Association of  Local Governments of  Nigeria (ALGON), 
which took place in Abuja in March 2021.  As part of  the 
resolutions of  the meeting, participants strongly canvass the 
establishment of  the NYSCTF as a dedicated Fund that will 
ensure adequate financing of  the operations of  NYSC to enable it 
 
xiv .    Establishment of  NYSC Museum
We have commenced work on the establishment of  the NYSC 
Museum, which will be domiciled at the National Directorate 
Headquarters. This is with a view to ensuring effective 
preservation of  the Scheme's records, artefacts and legacies, 
including Corps members' inventions and fabrications.

render required services to the nation.  If  actualized, the 
proposed NYSCTF will support adequate provision of  
infrastructural and other logistics for Orientation and other 
activities of  the Scheme. It will also help to make the Skill 
Acquisition and Entrepreneurship Development (SAED) 
programme more functional and provide start-up finances for 
Corps Entrepreneurs. The ripple effects will be such that the 
empowered Corps Members will in turn provide jobs for millions 
of  other Nigerians either through step-down of  vocational 
training or direct employment of  youths, especially those that are 
out of  school. The Fund will also ensure adequate provision of  
Corps Lodges, Transit Camps and other facilities essential for the 
welfare of  Corps members as well as for needs such as enhanced 
stipends and healthcare. I wish to, therefore, use this opportunity 
to once again appeal for the support of  the appropriate 
authorities towards the actualization of  the National Y outh 
Service Corps Trust Fund.
5. Given that participation in National Service is critical and 
compulsory for every eligible Nigerian graduate, there is need for 
them to be conversant with the objectives, programmes and other 
relevant issues concerning the NYSC. On this premise, 
Management is liaising with the Federal Ministry of  Education 
and the National Universities Commission for the inclusion of  
National Service as one of  the topics to be taught in the 'General 
Studies' Courses of  Corps Producing Institutions. This will help 
to prepare the Prospective Corps Members adequately for 
effective participation in the service.

years of  operation, the NYSC has been a remarkable success. By 
largely discharging its mandate through the nation's development 
objectives, the Scheme has become a national asset and a beacon

performing their duties.

Scheme adopt measures for the elimination of  all forms of  
hiccups militating against its operations through the 
intensification of  our engagement with critical stakeholders at the 
grassroots.

a. Conflicting Dates of  Graduation: It is disheartening 
to note that despite repeated appeals for honest handling 
of  roles, few of  us are bent on beating the system. As you 
are aware, the Scheme has commenced the inscription of  
dates of  graduation on the Certificate of  National 
Service. The steps taken to ascertain the actual dates of  
graduation have further exposed many Corps Producing 
Institutions that persist in this manipulation. 
Consequently , a large number of  graduates got stranded 
at various Camps during the 2021 Batch 'A' Stream II 
Orientation Course due to disparities in the dates of  
graduation on their Statement of  Results and the ones on 
the Call-up Letters. Despite these glaring anomalies, we 
compassionately decided to register the affected 
Prospective Corps Members while expecting their 
Institutions to make necessary corrections afterwards. 
However, I wish to strongly warn that such disparities will 
henceforth be treated as arising from deliberate acts of  
fraud that will be met with appropriate sanctions. 
will highlight the following the issues that have continued to be 
source of  concern: 
b. Imputation of  Academic Session Instead of  Y ear 
of  Graduation on Statements of  Result: This is a 
new dimension to manipulation by some Corps 
Producing Institutions. It is indeed curious that some 
institutions imputed academic session instead of  year of  
graduation on Statements of  Result.  Furthermore, cases 
of  reflection of  date of  issuance of  Statements of  Result 
as date of  graduation were also recorded as some 
prospective corps members attempted to register at the 
orientation camp with Statements of  Result carrying such 
misleading information. As you are already aware, the 
48
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL

c. Poor Quality of  Graduates : In line with an earlier 
resolution, we have put in place measures to identify 
schools with extremely poor quality of  graduates. The 
successful approach used in fishing out unqualified 
foreign-trained graduates have been modified to deal with 
home-trained graduates. Recently, two cases of   
graduates who were unable to write correct and simple 
sentences in English were discovered. Investigation is on-
going and the institutions involved would be temporarily 
sanctioned until satisfactory explanations are received 
regarding how those graduates got into their graduation 
lists. The responses of  the schools would determine our 
liaison with the appropriate regulatory bodies on the 
matter. Should this anomaly be traced to Data Entry , 
anyone responsible would be singled out for prosecution 
as provided for in the NYSC Act.
d. Persistent Discrepancies in the Names on Call-
Up Letters and Statements of  Result: It is 
noteworthy that despite repeated calls, many schools have 
date that is taken into account in determining eligibility 
for mobilization as provided in the NYSC Act is that of  
graduation. Therefore, in order to enforce the law , our 
Deployment and Relocation Officers will henceforth 
reject all graduates with such anomalies in their academic 
credentials. For the avoidance of  doubt, the date of 
graduation is the date the Senate or Academic 
Board approves the results  of the graduating 
students, and should, therefore, be the one on the 
Statements of  Result and Certificates.   Again, I 
would like to warn that any further manipulation of  dates 
will attract appropriate sanctions.

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
e. Increasing Cases of  Students Presenting 
Scanned Statements of  Result: With rapid advances 
in technology , manipulations and forging of  documents 
are becoming easier for people with fraudulent character. 
This is why we have continued to insist on presentation of  
original credentials for the purpose of  camp registration.  
In the past, incidences of  presentation of  scanned 
documents were regarded as individual isolated cases. It 
has, however, in recent time become worrisome because 
one of  the institutions sent its graduates to camps with the 
hope of  scanning their Statements of  Result for them to 
print on arrival. This was done even without prior notice 
to the NYSC Management. Although this has 
administratively been resolved, we have decided to 
mention it here so that it does not become rampant 
among institutions as it would no longer be condoned. 
f. Introduction of  Course of  Study on Certificate 
of  National Service: Another form of  manipulation 
which has continued to re-occur despite repeated 
warning is the disparity between the actual course of  
study of  the prospective corps members and the ones 
reflected on their Statements of  Result. This situation has 
continued to present candidates with discrepancies in the 
names on Statements of  Result and Call-up letters. This 
suggests lack of  synergy between those printing the 
Statements of  Result and officials feeding the 
Senate/Academic Board with data. The NYSC will 
continue to stop the registration of  prospective corps 
members with these discrepancies in order for the 
affected schools to accord the matter the seriousness it 
deserves.

g. Self-Correction of  Date of  Birth by Graduates:  
The recent introduction of  a window for prospective 
corps members to login and personally effect correction 
of  date of  birth using WAEC pin was with the objective of  
easing pressure on them. The procedures have already 
been outlined on the corps members' dashboard and 
Corps Producing Institutions have a duty to include this 
information in their communication platforms including 
general briefing of  prospective corps members. 
Institutions are to also sensitize and inform prospective 
corps members that any fraudulent change of  date of  
birth would be easily detected given the on-going efforts 
by the Government to streamline and manage data using 
the National Identity Management Commission 
(NIMC).
subjected the innocent graduates to untold hardship and 
psychological torture as they could not register for 
national service alongside their colleagues. For the 
avoidance of  doubt, prospective corps members with 
such cases will always be denied registration on camp. 
The Scheme will, in addition to this, re-introduce the 
reflection of  Course of  Study on Certificate of  National 
Service as was done previously .

Service Corps has zero tolerance for unethical practices and will

comply with extant procedures and guidelines on mobilization of

2. Distinguished ladies and gentlemen, you are all aware of  
the dynamic nature of  the world, which has since become a global 
village. In particular, there is increasing reliance on Information 
and Communication Technology (ICT) in the conduct of  
business by Government and Non-Governmental bodies 
worldwide.  Among other innovations, the Federal Government 
of  Nigeria initiated the cashless policy , which mandates the 
adoption of  Government Integrated Financial Management 
System (GIFMIS) as payment platform.  By this approach, all 
payments and budgetary processes are electronically-based, 
thereby increasing efficiency as well as enhancing probity and 
accountability in the management of  public funds. 
3. However, the cashless approach has also brought 
unintended consequences such as hacking of  data, spamming, 
ATM fraud, identity theft and other insidious acts.  In Nigeria, 
many bank depositors, including Government Agencies, have 
been victims of  the heinous activities of  hackers and crackers.  I

2.   In its forty-eight years of  existence, the NYSC has been 
discharging its mandate effectively despite the challenges and 
other realities of  the operating environment. It is on record that 
the Scheme has contributed immensely to the unity and 
integration of  Nigeria in addition to making significant impact on 
critical sectors of  the national economy such as health, education, 
agriculture and rural infrastructure. These, coupled with our 
participation in the implementation of  national programmes 
such as elections and the population and housing census, amongst 
others, have engendered deep appreciation of  the relevance of  
the NYSC by all Nigerians. In discharging its mandate, the 
Scheme has provided inspiration for other African countries, 
leading to the establishment of  the Y outh Service Schemes in the 
PROTOCOL

impacted positively on our operations thereby raising the profile 
of  the Scheme.

5.    It is almost two years now , when we had the last Annual 
Management Conference. This edition is coming at a time 
questions are raised on the continued relevance of  NYSC in some 
quarters. It is in this regard that the theme of  this year's 
Conference “The NYSC as a Catalyst for National Unity , 
Integration and Peaceful Co-Existence in Nigeria”  
becomes very apt. The issues singled out for the most scathing 
criticism are security of  Corps members and the deployment 
policy of  the Scheme. Although the vast majority of  Nigerians, 
who contributed to the discourse, endorsed and reaffirmed belief  
in the continued relevance of  the Scheme, these issues call for 
sober reflection and pragmatic actions. We must, therefore, use 
this forum to evolve effective strategies for tackling of  the issues so 
as to deepen the confidence of  serving and prospective Corps 
members, their parents and the rest of  the society . To this end, this 
conference will, amongst other highlights, feature lectures by 
experienced resource persons on the following topics:

the competence of  Staff  for higher productivity . Let me begin by

Officers for your commitment, especially through prompt

2.   Distinguished ladies and gentlemen, NYSC has remained 
committed to the successful implementation of  the FOI Act since 
it came into effect in 2011 in compliance with the Federal 
Government's directive on the domestication of  the Act by all 
Ministries, Departments and Agencies (MDAs). Another mark of  
our commitment is the fact that, among all MDAs, NYSC has the 
highest number of  FOIA Schedule Officers as could be seen in 
the roll call of  participants in this workshop.   This, coupled with 
our effective feedback mechanism, ensures prompt response to 
FOI requests and timely rendition of  annual reports to the 
Federal Ministry of  Justice over the years.

INTRODUCTION
Distinguished guests, ladies and gentlemen, I consider this 
invitation a great mark of  honour given the importance 
of  youth in the promotion of  security and peaceful co-
existence of  any nation. 
Mr. Chairman, other invited guests, assigning to me the topic, 
'The Significance of  NYSC Scheme to the Security and 
Peace Building in Nigeria: Prospects and Challenges', is 
no doubt the right call especially in view of  the pivotal role of  the 
National Y outh Service Corps, NYSC as a catalyst for change and 
national development. However, permit me to inform you that I 
have chosen to make a little amendment to the topic to read: 'The 
Significance of  the NYSC to Peace and National 
Development in Nigeria: Challenges and Prospects'.
As we may all be aware, the NYSC is one of  the foremost Y outh 
Organizations not only in Africa, but also the entire globe. It was 
established in 1973 with the objective of  fostering national unity 
and contributing towards accelerated development of  the 
Country , after the unfortunate civil war that divided the Country 
THE SIGNIFICANCE OF THE NYSC TO PEACE AND

2. THE ESTABLISHMENT OF THE NYSC 
Before I expatiate into the main discourse, it is imperative to draw 
our attention to the fact that useful as the youth is in driving the 
development of  any given nation, he can also be used willy-nilly 
in its destruction. This is perhaps, one of  the reasons why many 
Countries place emphasis on the development of  their youth. 
Nigeria is not left behind in this quest as the establishment of  the 
NYSC in 1973 was as a result of  the need to reconcile, reconstruct 
and rehabilitate the nation, which are all prerequisites for the 
sustenance of  peace, security and development in the country 
after the civil war. 
Even though a lot has been written about the interrelationship 
between security and nation building, one important aspect is still 
yet to gain the needed prominence – which is youth 
empowerment as it relates to peace and security of  any nation. 
To appreciate the NYSC, the history of  Nigeria especially the 
post-independence era must first be understood. This is because 
Nigeria is a country whose colonial history and experience has 
been characterized by ethnic loyalty , mutual group suspicion and 
distrust that led to a bloody Civil war from 1967 – 1970. Thus, the 
purpose of  the scheme is 'to inculcate in the Nigerian Y outh, the 
spirit of  selfless service to the nation and to emphasize the spirit of  
oneness and brotherhood of  all Nigerians, irrespective of  cultural 
and socio-economic backgrounds to promote National Unity and 
development.
along ethnic lines. Without mincing words, the Scheme has been 
able to achieve the main objectives of  its establishment, and has 
remarkably supported activities of  both Government and non-
governmental organizations, especially through the provision of  
critical manpower for nation building. 
101
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
i) To inculcate discipline in Nigerian youths by instilling in 
them a tradition of  industry at work and of  patriotic and 
loyal service to Nigeria in any situation they may find 
The National Y outh Service Corps scheme was established by nd
Decree 24 of  22  May 1973 as a deliberate effort to ensure the 
realization of  the policy of  Reconciliation, Rehabilitation and 
Reconstruction initiated by the Federal Government under 
General Yakubu Gowon after the Nigerian Civil War.  It aims to 
raise a new crop of  disciplined and detribalized Nigerians by 
allowing the youths to undergo national service in communities 
other than their own for the purpose of  national development 
and integration.  The Scheme was established with the view to 
promoting peace and encouraging mutual understanding of  the 
common ties among Nigerian youths thereby fostering national 
unity . The Decree as stated above was replaced by Decree 51 of  th
16  June 1993.  With the adoption of  the 1999 constitution which 
ushered in democratic rule, the enabling document establishing 
the NYSC is now referred to as “the NYSC Act CAP N84, Laws 
of  the Federation of  Nigeria 2004”. (NYSC, 2015). 
Objectives of  the NYSC Scheme
The Act makes it compulsory for all Nigerian graduates to 
participate in the one-year national service. It, however, excludes 
certain categories of  individuals such as graduates who are above 
thirty years of  age at the time of  graduation, graduates of  part-
time programmes/distance learning programmes, graduates 
who served for nine months and above and those currently 
serving in the Armed Forces, Police and other recognized para-
military services as well as recipients of  National Honours.
Against the historical experience of  Nigeria, the objectives of  the 
National Y outh Service Corps Scheme are spelt out in Section 
1(3a – f) of  the NYSC Act as follows;

themselves.
iii) To develop in the Nigerian youths, the attitudes of  
mind, acquired through shared experience and suitable 
training, which will make them more amenable to 
mobilization in the national interest.
v) To contribute to the accelerated growth of  the National 
economy .
Strategy for NYSC Scheme's Goal Realization
ii) To raise the moral tone of  the Nigerian youths by giving 
them the opportunity to learn about higher ideals of  
national achievement, social and cultural improvement.
viii) To develop a sense of  corporate existence and common 
destiny of  the people of  Nigeria (NYSC Act.).
iv) To enable Nigerian youths acquire the spirit of  self-
reliance by encouraging them to develop skills for self-
development.
vii) To remove prejudices, eliminate ignorance and confirm 
at first hand the many similarities among Nigerians of  
all ethnic groups; and
In order to achieve the objectives in sub section (3) of  the Act, the 
service corps shall ensure;
ii) That as far as possible, youths are assigned jobs in states 
other than their states of  origin.
vi) To develop common ties among the Nigerian youths 
and promote National unity and integration.
i) The equitable distribution of  members of  the service 
corps and the effective utilization of  their skills in areas 
of  National need.
iii) That such groups of  youths assigned to work together is 
as representative of  Nigeria as possible.
iv) That Nigerian youths are exposed to the modes of  living 
of  people in different parts of  the country .

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS

v) That the Nigerian youths are encouraged to eschew

differences.
vi) That members of  the service corps are encouraged to 
seek at the end of  their one-year National Service, 
career employment all over Nigeria, thus promoting the 
free movement of  labor.
vii) That employers are induced partly through their 
experience with members of  the service corps to employ 
more readily and on a permanent basis, qualified 
Nigerians, irrespective of  their States of  origin.
It is imperative to state that the Act provides a 3-tier structure for 
the funding of  the Scheme, i.e by the Federal, State and Local 
Governments. The State Governments are responsible for the 
provision of  Orientation Camps and accommodation for the 
Corps Members while the Local Governments are vested with the 
responsibilities of  ensuring the welfare of  the Corps Members at 
the grass-roots, including the provision of  adequate security .
The programmes of  the Scheme include the Orientation course 
which is designed to induct Corps Members and prepare them 
mentally and physically for the national service. After the 
orientation exercise, corps members are posted to Places of  
Primary Assignment, where they will be assigned schedules 
relevant to their areas of  specialization. Corps members are 
expected to carry out weekly Community Development Service 
in the host community where they are posted. At the end of  the 
service year, a passing out parade is organized to award the 
Certificate of  National Service to deserving Corps Members. 
The NYSC has offices in all the Seven Hundred and Seventy-
seven Local Governments Areas of  the Country .

3. THE SIGNIFICANCE OF THE NYSC TO PEACE, 
SECURITY AND NATIONAL DEVELOPMENT IN 
NIGERIA
It will therefore be safe to conclude that the youths in Nigeria play 
significant roles in the development of  the country . The period 
from 1965 to late 1970 saw the birth of  modern Nigeria with 
many developmental strides, including the establishment of  the 
nation's three refineries. The National Y outh Service Corps, 
which was established in 1973 is the brainchild of  the Yakubu 
Gowon Administration. During the period, many development 
plans as well as basic infrastructure in the Country were put in 
place in addition to the 1979 Constitution, which is a precursor to 
the current 1999 constitution. 
In examining the role of  youths in national development (as 
exemplified in the NYSC programme, it will not be out of  place to 
classify them as those who belong to the 'Gold' category in Plato's 
categorization of  ideal societies in one of  his famous books titled 
“The Republic”. According to Plato, the 'gold' category of  any 
given society are those who are intelligent and strong and whose 
roles should always be to give support in building the society . 
As mentioned in the opening part of  this paper, the non-
engagement of  the youths in positive and productive endeavours 
can make them idle and susceptible to unwholesome behaviours 
hence the question is, how best can the Nation encourage 
and promote youthful enterprise to a level where the 
youths become drivers of  our economic development? 
This is where the significance of  the NYSC to the security and 
national development in Nigeria becomes more incontestable. 
This paper will, therefore, focus on the successes of  the Scheme, 
which have greatly contributed to the security and stability of  the 
Country .
105

I. The Role of  the NYSC in the Fight Against 
COVID-19: Let me at this juncture inform this 
distinguished audience that the outbreak of  the Corona 
Virus pandemic presented opportunity for the young men 
and women undergoing national service to showcase their 
potentials. The NYSC used the period of  the lockdown to 
take series of  innovative measures aimed at ensuring that 
the abundant talents of  Corps members are harvested 
and channeled towards the fight against the pandemic. 
 The efforts of  corps members were severally commended 
by various State Governments, traditional rulers, 
community leaders and the Federal Government. 
 The above contributions, if  replicated by other youths will 
ultimately result in enhancing the security of  the country 
by engaging them in rewarding ventures. 
 While the country was under lockdown, corps members 
used their energies and innate talents to reach out to 
members of  their host communities through sensitization 
on the disease, its modes of  transmission and spread. 
They equally reached out to public spirited individuals to 
provide support for the less privileged citizens, in addition 
to the fabrication of  automated disinfection chambers, 
production of  Hand Sanitizers and Liquid Soap.  The 
corps members also produced face masks, which did not 
only receive wide acceptance across the Country , but also 
got the certification of  the Standard Organization of  
Nigeria, SON.  
ii. Reawakening the Spirit of  Patriotism and 
Contributing to National Development Among 
Nigerian Y ouths: As mentioned before, the NYSC was 
principally established to bring about national unity and 
development through instilling discipline, patriotism and

iii. T h e  N Y S C  S k i l l  A c q u i s i t i o n  a n d 
Entrepreneurship Development (SAED) Model 
as a Means of  Engaging the Y outh for Peace and 
National Development:  In furtherance of  our quest 
to pursue national integration and unity as well as 
contribute towards self-development of  youths and 
economic growth, the NYSC introduced the Skills 
Acquisition and Entrepreneurship Development (SAED) 
Department in 2012 in order to address graduate youth 
unemployment.  The programme is a veritable platform 
for the Scheme to contribute towards alleviating the 
problem of  graduate unemployment as well as changing 
the mindset of  our youths, which tends to be more 
inclined towards white collar jobs. While the fact remains 
that there are limited places in the labour market, 
especially for the fast-increasing graduate population, 
limitless opportunities abound for self-employment in the 
Nigerian economy through various programmes of  the 
Federal Government and other stakeholders. 
Through the SAED programme, the Scheme has 
succeeded in training Corps Members and raising from 
among them, skilled entrepreneurs, who have in turn, 
become employers of  labour. Therefore, if  the SAED 
model can be replicated right from the school level, it will 
ultimately help to raise more skilled youths in the Country . 
One peculiar nature of  the SAED programme is that the 
Corps beneficiaries are mandated to train at least five (5)

iv . The NYSC Agricultural and Ventures Initiative 
as a Means of  Providing Food Security and Y outh 
Employment:  Given the degree of  the Scheme's 
response to societal dynamics, the NYSC established 
Farms and V entures across the Country for the training 
and empowerment of  Corps Members with skills for self-
employment while also providing the immediate 
requirements of  the Scheme in terms of  Corps Members' 
kit items and basic feeding on camp. In this regard, NYSC 
Garment Factories were established in Minna, Niger 
State and Mgbakwu, Anambra State. The Scheme also 
established the NYSC Rice Mill Ezillo, Ebonyi State, and 
a Feed Mill in Lagos. In addition, we established NYSC 
Farms in Dungulbi, Bauchi State, Saminaka, Kebbi State, 
Kwali, FCT , as well as Iseyin, Oyo State. V ery recently , the 
Scheme has also established the NYSC Bakery and Water 
Factory in Kubwa, FCT Abuja.

vi. Sports and Entertainment as a Means of  
Engendering National Peace and Development:  
Currently , the National Y outh Service Corps has varied 
professional groups for different purposes. For instance, it 
has a Football Club which competes in the National 
League and a National Band, which performs in different

(NCAM), Leventis Foundation Nigeria, British American 
Tobacco Foundation Nigeria, among others. 
All these collaborations have not only trained our Corps

training of  yet another large number of  youths through 
the Corps members. After the training, they provide 
startup capital to the trained Agripreneurs.  The 
multiplier effect is that while these activities will benefit 
the nation in food sustenance, it will ultimately lead to 
employment and wealth creation.
v . Establishment of  NYSC Radio:  As part of  efforts of  
the NYSC to further enlighten the public on its activities 
and programmes, we have written and secured approval 
for the establishment of  NYSC Radio.  We are currently 
putting final touches to ensure the eventual take-off  of  the 
Radio Station.  The Station will be training ground for 
Corps Members that are interested in pursuing a career in 
the media industry .  It will also provide a platform for 
enlightening the public on the need for peaceful co-
existence and other government policies and 
programmes that require publicity .

vii. The NYSC Annual Sports and Cultural Festivals: 
The NYSC instituted the Sports and Cultural Festivals 
aimed at showcasing the talents of  Corps members in 
sports and culture and to serve as an additional platform 
for the promotion of  national unity and integration. This 
fiesta features competitions in football, volleyball and 
track events in the sports segment while the cultural 
segment involves contests in drama, cultural dance and 
comedy . Participants, who are usually Corps members 
from diverse backgrounds are given the opportunity to 
further interact and contribute towards the development 
of  their States of  service. It will interest this gathering to 
know that during these competitions, corps members 
represent their states of  service and not their States of  
origin. The beauty is the euphoria with which victories 
are celebrated by Corps members even when they win 
against their respective States of  origin in the 
competitions. 
The foregoing accomplishments notwithstanding, the NYSC like 
other organizations, grapples with some challenges, including the

4. SOME OF THE CHALLENGES FACED BY NYSC

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS

i. Increase in the Population of  Corps Members 
Amidst Dwindling Resources. It should be noted that the 
NYSC Act prescribes a tripartite arrangement for the operation 
of  the Scheme. However, other competing needs make funding to 
be inadequate. This hampers its operation, especially , in view of  
the steady and progressive increase in the number of  graduates 
being mobilized on annual basis. 
ii. Negative Publicity Against the Scheme.  It is no 
longer news that the NYSC has currently become the 'beautiful 
bride' whereby those who, for one reason or another are not 
interested in the peace and general well-being of  the Country 
resort to bashing the Scheme – particularly through the media.  
This may not be unconnected to the fact that some of  these critics 
attempted to circumvent the process and met a brick wall. The 
NYSC, which is the largest conglomerate of  youths in the 
Country as well as a driver of  social engineering for a self-reliant, 
united and prosperous nation, will not succumb to this cheap 
blackmail.
iii. Agitations/Attempts to Participate in the 
National Service by Unqualified Persons: It is important 
to mention here that one of  the challenges the NYSC is facing 
currently is attempt by unqualified persons especially those who 
claim to have attended foreign institutions, to participate in 
national service. As part of  efforts to stem this tide, the 
Management adopted several measures including physical 
verification of  credentials of  prospective Corps Members. 
During the verification exercises, some of  these graduates, who 
were reasonably suspected to possess fake certificates were 
subjected to further scrutiny . Such scrutiny often exposes the 
failure of  such graduates to read and write simple sentences. On 
further interrogation, they would confess to either having

Given the funding challenges earlier highlighted as

training and empowerment of  Corps members especially 
attended the schools at satellite campuses or paid for genuine 
certificates from the Institutions without physically attending the 
schools. Our efforts at curbing this trend has, however, led to 
agitations and resort to self-help by the affected persons through 
joining the calls for the scrapping of  the Scheme.  Let me 
therefore use this medium to call on the youth, especially through 
this forum, to assist members of  the public to critically study our 
NYSC Act with a view to understanding the workings of  the 
Scheme with particular reference to participation and evasion of  
service.  The Scheme is resolved more than ever before, to apply 
extant rules on persons that are against the provision of  the Act.
5. OUR PROSPECTS
Establishment of  the National Y outh Service 
Corps Trust Fund (NYSCTF):  It is noteworthy that 
in little over a decade since the start of  the Skills 
Acquisition programme of  the Scheme, Over One 
Million, Six Hundred Thousand Corps Members have 
been sensitized on entrepreneurship development with 
close to Eight Hundred Thousand receiving various levels 
of  training. Out of  this number, close to Twenty five 
Thousand have been linked to various financial 
institutions and other funding sources that have granted 
them loan facilities to the tune of  One Billion, One 
Hundred and Eighty-Four Million Naira.

6. CONCLUSION 
In conclusion, it can be seen that the Scheme, which came 
on board in 1973 has been a remarkable success in Nigeria. It 
demonstrates the fact that the youths can make meaningful 
contributions to national unity and development, if  their talents 
and skills are well harnessed. 
Given the above therefore, the Scheme has the prospects of  
generating more revenue for the Government and contribute to 
the nation's economic growth.
as part of  our contributions to the growth and development of  the

Government Treasury Single Account (TSA).
Thus, to quote from the writings of  Okpeh, (2021), the 
contributions of  the NYSC to the peace and development of  
Nigeria are as manifold as they are diverse, impressive, critical 
and relevant to our nation-building. The Scheme has relentlessly 
proved the point that the future of  the country belongs to the 
younger generations of  Nigerians who must be properly guided 
on the philosophy of  our corporate existence. 
Finally, if the youth are truly not too young to run, then 
certainly, they are not too young to contribute to the 
peace and development of the country.

2. The slave trade era was one of  the darkest and tragic 
periods defined by exploitation of  the human race. It was a period 
in which over fifteen million men and women of  African descent 
were traded and transported through the Atlantic, to be engaged 
in forced labour and subjected to other forms of  injustice. It took 
efforts and cooperation across the globe to bring an end to slave 
trade. 
   
3. Therefore, the declaration of  the International Day for 
the Remembrance of  the Slave Trade and its Abolition by the 
United Nations has helped in creating more awareness and raised 
our consciousness on the need to eschew racism and other forms 
of  discrimination. 
It is my pleasure to address you on this occasion of  the 
International Day for the Remembrance of  the Slave Trade 
and its Abolition. I consider my invitation to grace this special 
occasion as very apt given my background as a historian, and 
second, the critical role the National Y outh Service Corps has 
been playing in eliminating prejudices among Nigerian youths.

invitation for the second jab, where applicable. In addition, I 
charge you to help in sensitizing members of  the host 
communities about preventive measures, including the need to 
accept the vaccines.
7. Furthermore, I would like to reiterate our warning against 
unauthorized journeys and night trips. Statistics by relevant 
agencies have shown that night travel is a major risk factor for 
road traffic accident while such timing may also render rescue 
efforts fruitless. On this premise, it is now mandatory for all Corps 
members in transit to always cut short their trips from six o'clock 
in the evening and pass the night at military barracks and other 
locations officially designated as safe.  Y ou are also advised to 
board vehicles at approved motor parks to avoid falling prey to 
criminals disguising as commercial vehicle drivers.

one enough reason to believe they are either fake graduates or

shortcomings are always detected when they turn in applications

copy exact contents of  forms or other documents merely

 It has been discovered that some institutions operating in some 
West African countries engage in Certificate racketeering, with 
some also operating offshore campuses in Nigeria. In a bid to 
check the activities of  schools involved in this criminality , the 
NYSC often applies sanctions, including outright ban of  
Nigerian holders of  their Certificates from enlistment for 
National Service. Unfortunately , the blacklisted institutions 
would, in desperation, go ahead and trade their graduates for the 
purpose of  receiving Certificates from partner institutions. Part 
of  the measures we have taken to checkmate Nigerians, who 
patronize such citadels of  fraud, is our insistence on the 
presentation of  Ordinary Level Certificates, which are difficult to 
acquire fraudulently . This has gone a long way to check the 
incidents of  double registration on the NYSC Portal. The 
impunity of  the foreign institutions that sell fake Certificates has 
become so brazen because of  their collaboration with Nigerian 
agents, who help them to perpetrate this crime within our 
3. I am confident that all stakeholders gathered here today 
can work together to address the aforementioned and other 
related problems so as to avert their consequences on the socio-
economic progress of  our dear country .  Let me, therefore, seek 
your indulgence as I make further presentations on the following 
issues requiring specific regulatory or enforcement actions of  
specific organizations and the supportive roles of  other 
stakeholders along the value chain:
provided as specimen.  In many cases, the NYSC has been at the

ii. CERTIFICATES OF NATIONAL EXAMINATION 
BODIES
a) Cloning:  Many graduates are now able to clone 
Certificates issued by some of  these bodies with ease. 
c) Presentation of hand written O' Level results of 
Arabic and Islamic Studies: Many graduates are still 
presenting hand written O' Level statements of  results 
from Arabic and Islamic Studies Secondary Schools. 
b) Letters of  Confirmation of Lost Certificate : The 
confirmation letters come in different styles, sizes and 
patterns, thus casting doubt on their authenticity . Though 
some of  these Certificates can be verified online, the 
number of  graduates involved makes such exercise 
difficult to accomplish within the time frame for our 
Mobilization exercise. Even with the application of  online 
result checker, some questions still remain unanswered. 
For instance, we have duplicate copies of  a Certificate 
issued with different passport photographs to the same 
person. The online verification shows that the result is 
authentic, but it remains curious how two copies of  a 
Certificate could be issued with different photographs of  
the same holder. Of  course, only an investigation by the 
issuing authority can unravel this mystery .

iv . E X O R B I T A N T  F E E S  C H A R G E D  B Y 
PROFESSIONAL BODIES
It is understandable that professional bodies need to generate 
revenues to fund their activities. However, the exorbitant cost of  
obtaining and renewing licenses issued by some of  the bodies can 
have negative impacts. For instance, some prospective Corps 
members caught with forged professional papers explained that 
their actions were due to inability to afford the high fees charged 
and the desperation to, nonetheless, participate in the mandatory 
National Service. Similarly , long delays in the release of  the 
certificates and licenses after payment are not helping matters. 
Though a Scheme with humane disposition, we have always been 
compelled to send Prospective Corps members out of  our camps 
due to inability to present professional licenses, even with the risks 
associated with traveling.   I implore the affected bodies to also 
consider this, and fast track the process of  issuing practice licenses 
or certificates of  registration to their graduate members without, 
at the same time, compromising standards. 
v . M E D I C A L  R E P O R T S  I S S U E D  T O 
PROSPECTIVE CORPS MEMBERS
After careful analysis, we discovered that over ninety percent 
(90%) of  medical reports presented by prospective Corps 
members during registration at our Orientation Camps are fake. 
In 2015, we conducted comprehensive verification exercise in 
hospitals purported to have issued the medical reports in all the 36 
States of  the Federation and the FCT . Findings showed that many 
of  the papers actually emanated from the affected hospitals, but 
issued by unauthorized persons, including supporting staff, who 
received payments for the fake reports. This fraudulent act poses 
a great challenge for the NYSC as it makes it extremely difficult 
for us to identify Corps members with genuine health problems 
and take appropriate decisions regarding their deployment, 
welfare and participation in Orientation Camp activities. We are

iii. Ensuring that the scope of  evaluation by the Ministry goes

This will prevent the kind of  experience we had with a

141
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
It may interest this distinguished audience to know that the scale 
of  fraud has now escalated to the extent that stamps on 
international passports are also being faked. There are people, 
who have never left the country , yet their international passports 
are neatly stamped at different intervals to create the impression 
that they actually travelled out. Residence permits are also faked. 
Due to the ECOWAS free movement protocol, fraudulent 
persons seeking Mobilization for National Service also claim they 
used students' identity cards rather than international passports 
to travel and move around throughout the periods of  their 
purported study outside Nigeria. Thus, once they present 
residence permits, most of  which are ordinary typed sheets of  
papers, they are accepted as foreign-trained graduates without 
any documentary evidence of  their travel history . 
We have been reliably informed that the Ministry has 
commenced the process of  digitalizing the issuance of  evaluation 
letters, which will make forgery difficult. We wish to suggest that 
the barcodes introduced should be affixed on all letters issued. It is 
also advisable to have a uniform approach to the issuance of  the 
evaluation so as to avoid the situation where a single letter is issued 
to a school in respect of  an attached list of  graduates while

PROTOCOL
It is my pleasure to address you on this occasion of  the maiden 
edition of  the Grassroots Gender Sensitization and 
Advocacy Campaign, taking place simultaneously in rural 
communities across the Northern States. This campaign is a well 
thought out initiative of  the Reforms Unit of  the National Y outh 
Service Corps, which is implemented on the platform of  the 
Corps Gender Vanguards, with the aim of  exposing the ills of  
Gender-Based Violence (GBV). 
2. While gender issues are often misconstrued as affecting 
females alone, it is important to point out that they include 
matters of  interest to both sexes, including rights and 
responsibilities. In the past, some societies consider the female as 
weaker sex and tended to ascribe certain roles, which relegated 
them to the background. It has since become clear that some 
societal roles are not necessarily determined by our biological 
make-up and, therefore, can change with time and in different 
situations. It is also important to remind all and sundry that 
Gender Based-Violence is not only physical and psychological 
harm, but also constitutes abuse of  the fundamental rights of  the 
victim. Consequently , all hands must be on deck to fight this ill 
that is ravaging the society , especially in the rural dwellers.

It is my pleasure to address you on this occasion of  the Camp 
Managers' workshop organized by the General Services 
Department. We are grateful to God Almighty for bringing 
you safely to Abuja.
 Distinguished participants, as we are all aware, NYSC 
Orientation Camps are always the first port of  call for newly 
deployed Corps members. The condition of  these facilities will, 
therefore, leave a lasting impression on the Corps members. 
Despite the fact that the provision and maintenance of  
Orientation Camps are part of  the statutory responsibilities of  
the State Governments, Management is not unmindful of  its role 
in sustaining the positive image of  the Scheme.
As you may also be aware, the NYSC Orientation Camps across 
the country are facing several challenges ranging from the 
activities of  vandals, when camps are vacated; threats to security; 
and activities of  some members of  the host communities amongst 
others. The need to tackle these challenges, coupled with 
Management's commitment to building the capacity of  Staff  
make the conduct of  this workshop imperative.

For the avoidance of  doubt, date of  graduation is the date the 
Senate or Academic Board approves the result of  the graduating 
students and should, therefore, be the one on the Statements of  Result 
and Certificates. The position of  Management is that since 
schools are the ones supplying the data, the dates of  
graduation should appear on both the credentials and 
online/hard copy submitted to the NYSC. I, therefore, 
This default was glaring during the 2021 Batch 'B' Stream 
I Orientation programme, and after due consideration of  
the number of  Corps members stranded in our 
Orientation Camps, Management gave a concession of  
accommodating those found with disparity in what was 
uploaded on the portal and the Certificates issued five 
months before their mobilization. This type of  waiver 
will, however, not be given during the forthcoming 2021 
Batch 'C' Orientation course. 
I. Inclusion of  date of  graduation and course of  
study on NYSC Certificates: Y ou would recall that we 
recently introduced the policy on inclusion of  date of  
graduation and course of  study on the NYSC Certificate 
of  National Service and Certificate of  Exemption. We 
also issued circulars to schools notifying them that the 
policy would take-off  with effect from the 2021 Batch 'A' 
Service Year. That notwithstanding, many Corps 
members reported to the camp with discrepancies in their 
dates of  graduation after the notification. Also worrying is 
the way some institutions tend to confuse the date of  
graduation despite the fact that it was clearly defined 
during our last meeting and was reflected in the 
resolutions of  the meeting.

Although we have refrained from mentioning the names of  the 
various institutions involved in these infractions, those concerned 
have been approached privately . Now , we are determined to 
ensure that the offenders face the full wrath of  the law .   
11.  While we focus on correcting the identified anomalies, I 
will not forget to commend individuals and institutions, who have 
maintained the highest levels of  standard in the discharge of  their 
responsibilities. I enjoin all workshop participants to be fully 
dedicated to the tasks of  ensuring seamless and fraud-free 
mobilization process. 
12.  Thank you and God bless.

Protocol
I heartily congratulate the President Nigerian Army Officers' 
Wives Association (NAOWA), Management, Staff  and 
Students of  this great institution on the occasion of  your 
graduation ceremony .  In particular, I wish to congratulate the 
graduating students for adding another feather to your cap.  As in 
the old time cliché, many were called, but only a few made it to 
this day .  There is no gainsaying the fact that your graduation 
today is a testimony to your resilience over the years, through 
thick and thin.
2. Having completed your secondary education, you are 
now ready to move into the next level to unleash your potentials 
and actualize your dreams.  Fortunately , you have been privileged 
to attend one of  the most prestigious schools.  It is therefore 
expected that these experiences will prepare you more than any 
of  your peers to demonstrate that you are an asset to the nation.  It 
is a stepping stone for you to excel in your future educational 
endeavours.   Remember that your parents have invested in you 
so you must strive to ensure that you give them a return in 
investment.

3. My beloved children, allow me the privilege of  this 
opportunity to admonish you on the need to maintain the highest 
standard in the pursuit of  your future careers.  It is also important 
for you to know that there is no shortcut to success.  All successes 
achieved are as a result of  hard work, persistence and 
perseverance.
4. As you await admission into various higher institutions of  
learning, it is advised that you get yourself  engaged in productive 
ventures.  This is to avoid staying idle both physically and 
academically .  Y ou can start preparing and making yourself  
familiar with your dream course by embarking on advanced 
reading.
5. Let me also seize this opportunity to advise that you can 
also engage in endeavours in the area of  Skills Acquisition and 
Entrepreneurship Development through which you can develop 
skills that will provide opportunities for becoming self-reliant.  For 
instance, through our Skills Acquisition programmes, the NYSC 
has been able to produce thousands of  youth entrepreneurs as 
well as employers of  labour.  We have also been able to produce 
actors and actresses, athletes, stand-up comedians and movie 
producers through competitions in Our NYSC Sports and 
Cultural festivals.  All these are geared towards ensuring that the 
youth are positively engaged.  The NYSC has also produced a 
movie titled 'A Call to Service' where the Corps Members were 
exposed to the big stages through interaction with renowned 
Nollywood Actors and Actresses.
6. Similarly , you are to be reminded that your career choice 
at this level determine your success in the future.  From your 
parents, to the teachers, your seniors and indeed, all those before 
you, the choice of  right career affected who they turned out to be.  
Y ou should reflect on who you are and what you want to achieve.

PROTOCOL
I am highly delighted to welcome you all to this symposium on 
the proposed National Y outh Service Corps Trust Fund 
(NYSCTF) taking place in Abuja, the Centre of  Unity . Let 
me begin by recognizing the esteemed presence of  our Special 
Guest of  Honourable Minister of  the Federal Capital Territory , 
Alhaji Muhammad Musa Bello and the Guest of  Honour, the 
Honourable Minister of  Y outh and Sports Development, Mr. 
Sunday Dare.  Honourable Ministers, I cannot thank you enough 
for your sustained interest in the success of  the Scheme. I also 
welcome in a special way, the Chairman of  the Senate 
Committee on Y outh and Sports Distinguished Senator Obinna 
Ogba, Chairman Senate Committee on Army Distinguished 
Senator Muhammad Ali Ndume and the Chairman House of  
Representatives Committee on Y outh and Sports Honourable 
Y emi Adaramodu. In the same vein, I recognize the presence of  
the Chairman, NYSC National Governing Board, Ambassador 
Fatima Balla Abubakar and members of  the Board. To our guest 
speakers and other participants, I thank you for honouring our 
invitation to this forum. 
2. Honourable Ministers, distinguished ladies and 
WELCOME ADDRESS B Y THE DIRECTOR-G ENERAL, 
NYSC, B RIG G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN 
A T THE SY MPOSIUM ON THE IMPERA TIVE OF THE 
PROPOSED NA TIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
TRUST FUND HELD ON MONDA Y , 25TH
OCTOB ER, 20 21 A T BON HOTEL, ABUJA

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
4.  Over the years, the exponential rise in Corps population 
has brought with it the demand for commensurate allocation of  
resources. While the State and Local Governments have 
demonstrated commitment to the discharge of  their statutory 
obligations to the Scheme, other equally pressing needs seem to 
make the resource allocation inadequate. As a consequence, the 
Scheme contends with problems militating against its smooth 
operations, especially in the area of  provision of  start-up capital 
gentlemen, the essence of  this gathering is to engender a greater 
appreciation of  the imperative of  an NYSC Trust Fund and to 
generate ideas that will facilitate its actualization as well as the 
realization of  the set objectives. Like I have said on few occasions, 
the idea of  the Trust Fund came up while we were deepening the 
search for ways of  addressing challenges faced by the Scheme. I 
am confident that this symposium will result in further support for 
the proposal by all stakeholders.  
3. It may interest you to know that the Federal Government 
bears the heavier cost of  running the Scheme through feeding; 
medical services for Corps members and course officials during 
Orientation course; provision of  other logistics for Orientation 
and post-Orientation operations; payment of  Corps members' 
monthly Personal Allowances; payment of  Transport 
Allowances, provision of  Corps members' kit items; Insurance of  
Corps members as well as Staff  welfare and training, amongst 
others. On the other hand, Section 7, Sub-Sections 3 and 4 
as well as Section 8 of  the NYSC Act saddle States and Local 
Governments with complementary responsibilities such as 
provision of  befitting Orientation Camps, accommodation for 
Corps members, office accommodation for the NYSC State 
Secretariats as well as Zonal and Local Government Offices, land 
for agriculture, release of  State Subventions, security of  Corps 
members and support for the Scheme's Community 
Development Service.

for Corps members trained during the Skill Acquisition and 
Entrepreneurship Development programme (SAED), 
inadequate Orientation Camp facilities, inadequate 
accommodation for Corps members, non-release of  State 
Subvention by some State Governments and dwindling support 
for the Community Development Service.
5. Since my assumption of  office, I have made sustained 
advocacy engagement with stakeholders as part of  my policy 
thrust. Amongst other steps, we convened a meeting of  the NYSC 
Top Management with representatives of  State Governments, 
Federal Capital Territory Administration and the Association of  
Local Governments of  Nigeria in 2019 and 2021. Part of  the 
resolutions of  the 2021 meeting is the proposal for the 
establishment of  a dedicated fund that will be backed by law to 
complement resource allocation from the three tiers of  
government. The fund, which will be called the National Y outh 
Service Corps Trust Fund (NYSCTF) is expected to strengthen 
the operations of  the Scheme in the same manner the Tertiary 
Education Trust Fund, the Police Equipment Trust Fund and the 
Petroleum Technology Development Fund aid the operations of  
tertiary educational institutions, the Nigeria Police as well as the 
oil and gas industry respectively . 
6. W h e n  o p e r a t i o n a l ,  t h e  N YS C T F  w i l l  h e l p 
addressinfrastructural and other logistic needs for the smooth 
conduct of  Orientation Courses, provision Corps Lodges, Corps 
Transit Camps and other essential facilities for the welfare of  
Corps members. In addition, resources from the fund will support 
Staff  training for higher productivity as well as logistic 
requirements for special aspects of  our Community 
Development Service such as the medical outreaches conducted 
under the NYSC Health Initiative for Rural Dwellers. In a very 
significant way , the Fund will also focus on making the Skill 
Acquisition and Entrepreneurship Development (SAED)

that would emerge from the programme. The ripple effects of  this

potentials the hope of  a greater Nigeria rests.  As managers of  the

mandate.

PROTOCOL
I am highly delighted to address you on this occasion of  your 
formal induction into the National Y outh Service Corps. I 
rejoice with you on the successful completion of  your 
academic programmes, and your subsequent mobilization for the 
National Service. I also commend you for your prompt response 
to the clarion call to serve our fatherland. No doubt, history will 
be kind to you for your patriotic zeal.
2. As the launch-pad for the Service Y ear, this Orientation 
Course will prepare you physically and mentally for your 
expected contributions to the progress and development of  our 
fatherland. In addition, it will equip you for the realization of  your 
potentials and attainment of  individual feats both within the 
period of  service and beyond. Highlights of  the camp activities 
will include lessons on the four Cardinal Programmes of  the 
NYSC, leadership coaching, paramilitary drills and other 
physical trainings as well as sensitization on topical national 
issues, amongst others. Y ou are expected to avail yourselves of  this 
unique opportunity by participating actively in all the 
aforementioned programmes.

3.  In line with some of  the objectives of  the NYSC, we 
deliberately posted you away from your States of  origin in 
addition to assembling you here from diverse ethnic, religious and 
socio-economic backgrounds. These deployment policies are 
aimed at broadening your understanding of  the country , thereby 
standing you in good stead for effective contribution to the 
promotion of  national unity and integration. I, therefore, 
encourage you to ensure healthy interactions, exchange ideas and 
build lasting friendships with a view to advancing the progress of  
a united Nigeria.  
5. While commending you for having conducted yourselves 
well so far, I encourage you to continue to demonstrate high level 
of  discipline and enthusiasm throughout the exercise. Let me also 
remind you that the regimented nature of  the Camp is intended 
to further instill discipline and build your resilience. Y ou are 
expected to comply strictly with the set rules and regulations and 
be obedient to your course officials.
4. My dear compatriots, today , you have taken the solemn 
oath to dedicate yourselves to the service of  our fatherland. I 
enjoin you to always ponder over the significance of  the oath and 
be guided by its spirit and letters. In the same vein, I advise you to 
familiarize yourselves with the content of  both the NYSC Act and 
the NYSC Bye-Laws. 
6. Let me use this opportunity to caution you against 
indulgence in cultism, drug abuse and other social vices.  I also 
urge you to use the social media only for the promotion of  unity 
and other positive purposes rather than rumour peddling and the 
promotion of  hatred. At all times, you must be security conscious, 
and avoid putting yourselves in harm's way .

8. At this juncture, I wish to remind you of  the need to 
continue to comply with the COVID-19 prevention protocols 
throughout the Orientation period. In particular, you must 
ensure physical distancing and wearing of  face masks as well as 
make good use of  hand washing facilities provided at strategic 
locations, amongst other safety measures. As you may be aware, 
the Federal Government has announced plan to make 
presentation of  evidence of  COVID19 vaccination by civil st
servants a pre-requisite for gaining entry to public offices from 1  
December, 2021. I, therefore, encourage those of  you, who are 
yet to take the vaccine, to do so without further delay as the rule 
will apply to Corps members in places of  Primary Assignment. 
Of  greater significance is the fact that the vaccine will keep you 
safe. We are already in touch with the relevant authorities with a 
view to ensuring that the vaccines are made available to you in the 
course of  this programme.
7. It is no longer news that white collar jobs are hard to come 
by . For this reason, the empowerment of  Corps members for self-
employment and wealth creation has been a major area of  focus 
for the Scheme since 2012. Y ou will from this moment be availed 
of  that opportunity through our Skill Acquisition and 
Entrepreneurship Development (SAED) programme. I am 
happy to inform you that many of  your predecessors, who 
embraced vocational and entrepreneurial training on the SAED 
platform, are now successful business owners. I, therefore, 
encourage you to stay off  the long queue of  job seekers by 
choosing from the various skill sets and participating fully in the 
training sessions. On our part, we shall continue to work with 
relevant stakeholders, including financial institutions, to enable 
you actualize your business dreams. 
9. Once again, I would like to express our profound

2. Let me also place on record, our appreciation for the

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
2. My dear compatriots, as you begin the next phase of  the 
Service Y ear, I urge you to sustain the spirit of  patriotism, hard 
work and resilience, which you imbibed during the Orientation 
Course. It is my ardent hope that you will strive to meet the 
expectations of  Nigerians by contributing towards the progress 
and development of  our fatherland.
PROTOCOL
3. Y our letters of  posting to Places of  Primary Assignment 
will be handed to you soon after this ceremony . In this regard, I 
would like to remind you of  your oath of  allegiance in which you 
pledged to accept posting in good faith. I enjoin you to perform 
your duties with diligence and be guided by the provisions of  the 
NYSC Act and Bye-Laws as well as workplace rules and 
I am pleased to address you as the 2021 Batch 'C' Stream I 
Orientation Course comes to a close today . First, I thank 
Almighty God for the success of  the programme. I also 
commend your patriotic zeal as demonstrated through active 
participation in Camp activities and exhibition of  high level of  
discipline.  
ADDRESS BY THE DIRECTOR-GENERAL, NYSC, 
BRIG GEN S IBRAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN 
A T THE TERMINAL PARADE/CLOSING CEREMONY 
OF THE 2021 BA TCH 'C' STREAM I ORIENT A TION 
COURSE HELD ON TUESDAY , 
9th NOVEMBER, 2021
