A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
regulations. In keeping with the objectives of  the Scheme, you are 
expected to integrate into your host communities while also 
appreciating and respecting their cultures. I must,however, 
emphasize that engagement in their local politics is a no-go-area 
for you.  Furthermore, I enjoin you to undertake personal and 
group Community Development Service projects that will help to 
uplift the living standard of  the people.
4. I have received impressive reports on your participation in 
the entrepreneurial and vocational trainings conducted in Camp 
under the NYSC Skill Acquisition and Entrepreneurship 
Development (SAED) programme. I encourage you to build on 
the skills acquired by availing yourselves of  opportunities for post-
camp training. This will go a long way in empowering you for self-
employment. On our part, we are liaising with financial 
institutions and other stakeholders with a view to providing start-
up loans to enable you actualize your business dreams. I wish to 
assure you that Management will continue to explore avenues for 
optimizing the impact of  the programme. 
6. At all times you should be good ambassadors of  the 
NYSC as well as your families and institutions of  graduation. 
5. My dear Corps Members, as you proceed to your 
locations of  Primary Assignment, I urge you to be security 
conscious at all times. Steer clear of  acts that can put you in 
harm's way such as staying out late night, attendance of   night 
parties, visitation of  dangerous places, and acceptance of  car ride 
from strangers. Y ou can rest assured that Management remains 
committed to your security and general welfare.  Accordingly , we 
are in constant liaison with security agencies and other 
stakeholders with the view of  ensuring your safety as well as 
addressing other essential needs for a fulfilling service year.
242
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
8. At this juncture, I would like to reiterate our warning 
against unauthorized journeys and night trips. Travelling at night 
will not only increase the risk of  accident, but also make rescue 
difficult.Y ou are, therefore, advised to always cut short your trips 
from six o'clock in the evening and pass the night at military 
barracks and other locations officially designated as safe.  
Furthermore, you should board vehicles only at approved motor 
parks so as to avoid falling prey to criminals. 
Therefore, you must be wary of  acts that can soil our image, 
especially vices such as drug abuse and trafficking, cybercrime 
and advanced-fee-fraud. Also remember that your membership 
of  the Service Corps does not confer immunity from the legal 
consequences of  any wrongdoing.  I, therefore, enjoin you to 
continue to be law-abiding while also serving as role models for 
the younger ones.
7. I urge you to avoid using the social media for ethnic 
jingoism, rumour peddling and the promotion of  hatred. Instead, 
your activities online should be targeted at self-improvement as 
well as promotion of  the unity , peace and prosperity of  our dear 
country . Also avoid being speculative on issues affecting the 
NYSC and, instead, visit our website, social media platforms and 
other official channels for clarifications.    
9.       Let me use this opportunity to remind you that the 
COVID-19 prevention protocols are not meant to be observed in 
the Orientation Camp alone.  With your level of  awareness of  the 
virus, I am confident that you would continue to be on your guard 
everywhere you find yourselves while also helping to sensitize 
members of  the host communities. May I also remind you of  the 
Federal Government's plan to make presentation of  evidence of  
COVID-19 vaccination a condition for gaining entry to 
243
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
10.    I consider it appropriate to once again appeal to Corps 
Employers to always accept Corps Members posted to them, and 
make the necessary provisions for their welfare. In addition, I urge 
you to mentor them properly to enable them develop their 
potentials. I also call on other stakeholders, including State and 
Local Government authorities as well as traditional rulers, to give 
the necessary encouragement to the Corps members. 
12. Finally , it is now my pleasure to declare the 2021 Batch 'C' 
Stream I Orientation Course closed. I wish you a very impactful 
and rewarding service year.
13.  Thank you and God bless.
11. I will not end this address without thanking the Federal 
Government for its unwavering support for the Scheme. Our 
appreciation also goes to State Governments, Local Government 
Councils, Security Agencies, the Presidential Steering 
Committee on COVID-19, the Nigeria Centre for Disease 
Control, the National Agency for the Control of  AIDS, the TY 
Danjuma Foundation, traditional rulers, Corps Employers and 
other stakeholders whose support has contributed to our 
successes over the years.
st 
government offices from 1 December, 2021.  Y ou are, therefore, 
expected to make yourselves available for the vaccination as the 
rule will apply to you in your places of  Primary Assignment.

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
It is with immense pleasure that I address you on this occasion 
of  the 2021 edition of  the Corps Employers' Workshop 
taking place simultaneously in all the 36 States of  the 
Federation and FCT . This programme serves as an avenue for 
exchange of  ideas on the improvement of  our operations, 
especially through the provision of  enabling environment for 
Corps members to render qualitative and efficient services.  In 
fulfillment of  its objectives, the NYSC is promoting national unity 
and accelerated socio-economic development of  the nation as 
well as instilling in our youths a tradition of  industry at work and 
of  patriotic and loyal service to Nigeria amongst other activities.  
The achievement of  these and other objectives can only be 
sustained through the collective efforts of  all stakeholders, 
including the managers of  the Corps members.

of  Corps members for a substantial part of  the year just as it 
temporarily affected the utilization of  the serving ones by some 
Corps Employers. However, the pandemic provided opportunity 
for the NYSC to once again assert its continued relevance 
through the harnessing of  the knowledge, skills and talents of  our 
young men and women on National Service. Accordingly , while 
the nation was on lockdown, the Scheme remained very visible as 
we mobilized Corps members to make various interventions in 
support of  the overall national efforts to contain the virus. Apart 
from the Corps Medical Teams that provided health care services 
in various health facilities, other Corps members made their 
impact felt through the following:
· Donation of  food and other palliative items to indigent 
persons;
· Mass production and donation of  face masks, antiseptic 
liquid soaps and hand sanitizers through the FCT 
Administration and State Governments all over the 
Federation; 
· Fabrication and donation of  automatic and foot-operated 
water, liquid soap, hand sanitizer dispensers and 
disinfection chambers in several States;

5. In the light of  the foregoing, I would like to remind you of  
the expected roles of  Corps Employers in the effective 
implementation of  the Cardinal Programmes and other activities 
of  the NYSC. The following are some of  our expectations during 
the different phases of  the Service Y ear: 
ii. Primary Assignment:  Before commencement of  
Orientation Course, Corps Employers are expected to 
submit requests for Corps members stating the number, 
discipline and other specifications that will assist the 
Scheme in carrying out postings to places of  Primary 
Assignment. At this juncture, I wish to remind you of  a 
subsisting circular from the Federal Government, which 
prohibits rejection of  Corps members by Government 
Ministries Department and Agencies (MDAs). To this 
end, I wish to appeal to all Corps employers, especially 
Government Establishments, to make adequate 
budgetary provisions for the welfare of  Corps members 
rather than rejecting them. 
i. Orientation Course: The comfort of  Corps members 
during the Orientation programme is one of  the key 
Corps Welfare provisions. Accordingly , Management has 
continued to sensitize State Governments on the need to 
provide adequate facilities in the Camps. We have also 
been carrying out advocacy for States and Local 
Governments to provide Transit Camps and Corps 
Lodges in all the 774 Local Governments Areas in the 
country . We expect employers to also join in this advocacy 
and, where you have provisions for Corporate Social 
Responsibility , always endeavour to assist in the provision, 
maintenance or upgrade of  the aforementioned facilities.

iv . Approval of  leave/journeys: Let me also remind you

has been recording great success in the biometric 
registration and clearance of  Corps members and, in the 
process, made perpetration of  unwholesome practices 
extremely difficult.  Management has also increased the 
regularity of  our inspection of  Corps members at their

iii. Welfare of  Corps members:  In the course of  the 
Primary Assignment, which is the second phase of  the 
Service, employers are expected to make some statutory 
welfare provisions for the Corps members.  These include 
transportation from camp, reception/induction on 
arrival at the service location, accommodation with 
modest furnishing, transport to and from office or a 
reasonable amount of  money in-lieu of  same as well as 
free medical services and local allowances, amongst 
others.  No doubt, these will be veritable sources of  
motivation for the Corps members, and will go a long way 
to engender productivity.  The employers are also 
expected to apply appropriate sanctions against Corps 
members when they err as well as report details of  
wrongdoing and actions taken to the Scheme.

hand with the Primary Assignment and is compulsory for 
all Corps members.  It serves as a platform for

the host communities.  I wish to appeal to Corps 
Employers to assist the Corps members both in the 
provision of  resources and in the mobilization of  support 
from members of  the public towards execution of  
projects for the benefit of  the host communities.

2.  On my assumption of  office as Chief  Executive of  the 
NYSC, I observed the communication gap between the Scheme 
and foreign Corps Producing Institutions. Also worrisome were 
the unimaginable malpractices perpetrated by some of  the 
institutions, especially those within West Africa. The most 
shocking aspect was the outright sale of  Degree Certificates to 
persons, who never attended the institutions. Persons in this 
category are unable to display basic reading and writing skills or

here, I wish to present for discussion,  the following problems 
identified with foreign Corps Producing Institutions:
(a).   Award of Short Service Degrees: The award of  short 
service degrees to interested clients is an invention of  
criminal elements, who are in pursuit of  pecuniary gains. It 
has been discovered that many foreign institutions run 
three to six-month degree programmes operated under the 
guise of  transferred credit from other institutions. They do 
not follow any established procedure of  receiving credits 
from the previous schools, neither do they open any form 
of  communication with the candidates' former institutions. 
This gives room for drop-outs from Nigerian institutions to 
cross over to these countries supposedly for studies and 
graduate before their former mates. Managers of  some of  
the schools involved give the flimsy explanation that

Subsection 5 states that:
“where an offence under subsection (3) of  this section which has 
been committed by a body corporate, is proved to have been committed 
with the consent or connivance of  or to be attributed to any neglect on

3. As you may be aware, the SAED programme came into 
being in 2012 as a platform for the National Y outh Service Corps 
to contribute towards tackling the challenge of  unemployment 
amongst our teeming graduate youths. Of  course, there is no 
gainsaying the fact that the panacea against this challenge is to 
steer the mindset of  our youths away from the mirage of  white 
collar job to that of  entrepreneurial engagement. As a Scheme, 
we consider this as even more compelling in view of  the fact that 
the period of  National Service is designed to serve as a buffer for 
youths as they transit from school life to the realities of  the 
mainstream society . Thus, we have continued in our strides for the 
success of  the programme with the support of  partners such as 
the Bank of  Industry, Access Bank, Unity Bank, Leventis 
Foundation Nigeria, British-America Tobacco Foundation and 
others too numerous to mention. Parts of  the gains of  our 
collaborations are empowerment of  Corps members with 
financial grants and loans for the actualization of  their business 
plans as well as the establishment of  zonal skills training centres 
across the country .
4. I am happy to inform this gathering that Corps members 
in successive batches have shown more than a passing interest in 
the SAED programme. Many have been able to establish and 
successfully nurture their own businesses. This Festival is thus a 
celebration of  the evolving success of  the programme. In

Out of  these, seven hundred and sixty-four thousand six hundred

and entrepreneurship training while up to eighteen thousand six

self-help, Bank loans and grants from donors.  We have been 
showcasing our success stories in our now popular TV 
programme, “NYSC Half  Hour” on NTA International, 
Channel 251 every Wednesday , at 7.30 pm, where our Corps  
beneficiaries give testimonies.  Interestingly, 95% of  the 
beneficiaries established their enterprises in their States of  
service, not their States of  origin.  We have also created the NYSC 
CV Bank and Jobs Portal (www .nyscjobs.ng), which provides an 
interactive platform for employers and prospective employees, 
especially for those who are still inclined to making contributions 
to various sectors of  the economy through white collar jobs.

9. This, however, is against the provisions of  the NYSC Act, 
particularly Section 2 Subsection 1 of  the Act which provides that 
every Nigerian shall, be under an obligation, unless exempted 
under Section 2 Subsection 2 of  the Act or Section 17 of  the Act, 
to make himself  available for service for a continuous period of  
one year from the date specified in the call-up instrument served 
upon him. Subsection 2 of  the same section also states further that 
notwithstanding the provisions of  Subsection 1 of  the section, st
with effect from 1  August 1985, a person shall not be called upon 
to serve in the Service Corps if  at the date of  graduation or 
obtaining his diploma or other professional qualification (s) or he 
is over the age of  thirty years. 
8. Let me use this opportunity to appeal to Corps Producing 
Institutions (CPIs) not to fail in sending forward their qualified 
graduates for National Service upon graduation as delay in 
presenting them can lead to their disenfranchisement. This is 
because the affected persons could cross the age limit of  thirty (30) 
years as provided for in the Act. These delays are usually caused 
by the inability of  the Institutions to conclude necessary 
clearance and mobilization processes that leave the affected 
graduates waiting longer than necessary before being mobilized.

4. As you are all aware, recent happenings reveal that 
hackers could install several programmes on your system without 
your knowledge. Such programmes could be used to steal 
sensitive information such as password and credit card details as 
well as import files from your systems. Since the NYSC financial 
systems rely wholly on GIFMIS/REMITA platforms, the weight 
and consequences of  criminal infiltration of  the system will be 
devastating for the Scheme. Given the phenomenal rise and 
sophistication of  cyber-criminality in our financial space, I wish 
to call for eternal vigilance and caution by all NYSC officers 
dealing with this payment technology .
5. All hands must be on deck to safeguard our financial 
system from fraudulent activities. As custodians of  the Scheme's 
treasury , you must display at all times, the highest standard of  
professionalism, integrity and transparency in the discharge of  
your duties. 
6. I would like to conclude by reaffirming Management's 
commitment to upholding, promoting and protecting core 
financial values and principles that will deepen accountability 
and transparency in the overall financial administration of  the 
NYSC. I am confident that you will also key into our vision of  
bequeathing a financially resilient and stable Scheme.
7.  On this note, it is my pleasure to declare this training workshop

NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
PROTOCOL
I warmly welcome you all to the opening ceremony of  the 
2022 NYSC Annual Management Conference (AMC) taking 
place here in Abuja, the Centre of  Unity. I thank the Almighty 
God for granting all our guests and participants journey mercies.  
Let me specially welcome our Special Guest of  Honour and 
Honourable Minister of  the Federal Capital Territory , Mallam 
Muhammad Musa Bello, and the Guest of  Honour, the 
Honourable Minister of  Y outh and Sports Development, Mr. 
Sunday Dare.  I thank you most sincerely for honouring us with 
your esteemed presence in spite of  your tight schedule. In the 
same vein, I appreciate the Chairman and members of  the 
NYSC National Governing Board and all other distinguished 
guests, who have come from far and near to grace this occasion.
 
2.  Honourable Ministers, distinguished guests, ladies and 
gentlemen, the Annual Management Conference is a forum 
where the NYSC Top Management and other key officers make 
critical review of  the Scheme's operations with a view to evolving 
new policies and strategies for improved performance.  As you are 
all aware, the COVID-19 pandemic affected the operations of  
not only the NYSC, but also all other organizations globally .  
However, despite the challenges posed by the pandemic, the 
WELCOME ADDRESS BY THE DIRECTOR-GENERAL, 
NYSC, MAJ GEN S IBRAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN 
M TRCN A T THE OPENING CEREMONY OF THE 
2022 NYSC ANNUAL MANAGEMENT CONFERENCE, 
ON WEDNESDA Y , 26TH JANUARY , 2022 A T 
ZEUS P ARADISE HOTEL, MABUSHI ABUJA

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
3. Y ou will agree with me that since its establishment in 
1973, NYSC has continued to play vital roles in areas of  national 
unity and integration, promotion of  peaceful co-existence among 
people of  different socio-cultural backgrounds, and free 
movement of  labour among others.  The contributions of  the 
Scheme to national development, particularly in the areas of  
health, education, rural infrastructure, culture and tourism, 
sports, conduct of  elections and job creation have attracted 
commendations from within and outside the country . Detailed 
documentation of  these and other contributions have been made 
in nine books, which we published and unveiled to the public last 
year. The Scheme's accomplishments are also being showcased 
through our in-house news magazine, print and electronic media 
and the newly established NYSC Museum/Archives.
Scheme has continued to operate effectively in line with the 
established safety protocols. We have been working closely with 
the Presidential Steering Committee on COVID-19, the Nigeria 
Centre for Disease Control as well as Federal and State Ministries 
of  Health for safe and efficient conduct of  Orientation Courses 
and other aspects of  our operations. I am glad to mention that the 
Scheme has become a reference point for other organizations due 
to the measures we put in place in response to the pandemic. 
4. While we appreciate stakeholders' roles in the 
achievements recorded so far, this forum seeks to consolidate 
them by generating new ideas for greater impact.  This informed 
the choice of  the theme of  the conference, “Repositioning the 
NYSC for Improved Healthcare Delivery, Revenue 
Generation and Corps Employment for Self-Reliance.” 
It underscores our sustained commitment to the success of  the 
NYSC mandate and continued contribution to national 
development. In addition to brainstorming on various issues, 
lectures will be presented by experienced resource persons on 
topics relevant to the theme.
296
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
5. Honourable Ministers, distinguished guests, permit me to 
state that despite the aforementioned achievements, the Scheme 
still faces some challenges.  These arise mainly from non-
discharge of  statutory responsibilities by some critical 
stakeholders. Problems such as dilapidated Orientation Camp 
facilities, inadequate Corps Lodges and lack of  befitting office 
accommodation are being contended with in some States. 
Another area of  concern has to do with the provision of  start-up 
capital for Corps members after acquisition of  entrepreneurial 
skills.
6. As we continue to call on the relevant stakeholders to help 
in addressing the foregoing challenges, I wish to also use this 
medium to appeal to the appropriate authorities and well-
meaning Nigerians to support the establishment of  the proposed 
NYSC Trust Fund.  Among other benefits, the Fund will make 
the Skill Acquisition and Entrepreneurship Development 
(SAED) Programme of  the Scheme more impactful through 
provision of  training facilities and start-up capital for Corps 
entrepreneurs. It will also assist in addressing our infrastructural 
needs for enhanced operational efficiency .  I am delighted to note 
and inform this gathering that the Bill has scaled second reading 
in the House of  Representatives.
7. At this juncture, I would like to express our sincere 
gratitude to the Federal Government for its continuous support 
for the NYSC, especially through the prompt release of  funds for 
the smooth conduct of  our operations.  I wish to also extend our 
appreciation to the Honourable Minister of  Y outh and Sports 
Development, the Honourable Minister, Federal Capital 
Territory , as well as the Chairman and Members of  the NYSC 
National Governing Board for your continuous support.  In the 
same vein, I thank all our invited guests, including gentlemen of  
the press, for your presence.
8. Thank you and God bless.

It is my pleasure to welcome all participants to the Business 
Session of  the 2022 Annual Management Conference. Let 
me begin by appreciating you for your shared commitment 
and hard work, which resulted in the successes recorded by the 
Scheme over the years. 
2. Since establishment in 1973, the NYSC has been 
operating effectively even in the midst of  daunting challenges.  It 
is on record that the Scheme has impacted greatly on the socio-
economic development of  Nigeria through its various 
programmes.  Our contributions to the real sectors of  the nation's 
economy , including education, health, agriculture and rural 
infrastructure are very visible, and have been profoundly 
appreciated by Nigerians.  In the same vein, our participation in 
the implementation of  national programmes such as elections, 
population census and mass sensitization of  the rural populace 
have earned the Scheme a lot of  accolades.
3.  As you are aware, the present Management has left no 
stone unturned in efforts to further enhance the relevance of  the 
Scheme, especially in the face of  prevailing socio-economic 
realities. Y ou would recall that on assumption of  duty , I unveiled

7. At this juncture, I would like to present the following 
agenda, which will form the basis of  our discussion in this forum:
a. Reinvigoration of  the Health Initiative for Rural 
Dwellers: The intervention of  the Scheme in the health sector 
through the Health Initiative for Rural Dwellers is achieving the 
desired objective. Amongst other improvements made, we have 
increased the frequency of  the nationwide medical outreach 
within the year as the programme is now carried out on quarterly 
basis. It is pleasing to note that more than Four Hundred 
Thousand (400,000 ) persons were attended to during our 
outreaches in 2021 alone, and this has elicited applause from 
various stakeholders. We have equally introduced the idea of  
forwarding analysis of  the ailments treated in each State to 
respective State Governors to help in their healthcare delivery 
programme.  I wish to emphasize the need to improve on the feats 
achieved so far in the efforts to enhance our health services to 
rural communities. Accordingly , State Coordinators are directed 
to step up liaison with relevant stakeholders such as State Primary 
Healthcare Agencies and pharmaceutical companies for support, 
especially through provision of  drugs and other medical 
disposables.
b. Reinvigoration of  the Skill Acquisition and 
Entrepreneurship Development (SAED) Programme : 
The completion of  Skill Acquisition Centres in Gombe, Katsina, 
Jigawa, Ogun and Nasarawa States is part of  the new vistas for 
reinvigoration of  the SAED programme. The Centres will enable

It is with immense delight that I welcome you all to the official 
commissioning of  the ultra-modern NYSC Museum of  great 
History , domiciled at the National Directorate Headquarters 
of  the Scheme. I am particularly pleased to welcome the 
Honourable Minister of  Y outh and Sports Development, Mr. 
Sunday Dare, who has always been very supportive to the 
Scheme.  In the same vein, I welcome the Chairman, NYSC 
National Governing Board and other invited guests for gracing 
this historic occasion.
2. Honourable Minister, distinguished guests, ladies and 
gentlemen, my background as a Historian made me appreciate 
the need for the documentation of  the activities of  the Scheme. 
This gave rise to a number of  activities, including the unveiling of  
nine (9) books and other publications on the activities and 
successes recorded by the Scheme among other documentation 
processes. The establishment of  the NYSC Museum is, therefore, 
is a continuation of  this process.  
3. The need for a museum as repository of  historical and 
archival materials for an organization with such a rich history of  
ADDRESS BY THE DIRECTOR-GENERAL, NYSC, 
MAJ GEN SHUAIBU IBRAHIM, DSS ASOC. PROF . 
MTRCN, FHSN, FNARC A T THE INAUGURA TION

MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN

close to five decades cannot be overemphasized. The NYSC 
Museum of  Dynamic History , therefore, showcases this rich 
history from the inception of  the Scheme in an attempt to preview 
the future.  Archival materials in this museum have also been 
documented in the print and electronic media to make them 
more accessible to the general public.
4. Honourable Minister, distinguished guests, the Scheme 
had the privilege of  conducting some personalities round the 
Museum at its take-off  stage. It has been visited by prominent 
national and international personalities, notable among whom 
are the Nasarawa State Governor, the Indian High 
Commissioner to Nigeria, President of  the United Nations 
General Assembly, Commandant General, NSCDC, Force 
Commander, Multinational Joint Task Force (MNJTF), members 
of  National Assembly and traditional rulers from across the 
country , among others. The positive comments from these 
individuals is a testimony to the fact that the establishment of  the 
museum is long overdue given the unparalleled success recorded 
by the NYSC over the years.
5. Artworks, painting, fabrications and innovations of  Corps 
members, and the non-pharmaceutical materials they produced 
in support of  the war against COVID-19 have all been 
adequately preserved in this museum. I am happy to report that 
our effort to preserve history of  the Scheme has received so much 
support as individuals have been forwarding to donate artefacts 
and other materials produced during their service years to the 
museum.   
6. It is our hope that individuals including researchers will 
find in the Museum, valuable source of  reference materials on the 
contributions of  the Scheme to the national development. We

3.   The major challenges of  the SAED programme cannot be 
overemphasised. They include inadequate skill training facilities, 
inadequate finance for business start-up  and insufficient access to 
mentorship and counselling. In the face of  dwindling budgetary 
resources, we are convinced that these challenges can be 
effectively tackled by the emergence of  more bilateral and 
multilateral collaborations with the private sector organizations. 
It is my hope, therefore, that the deliberations at this forum will 
lead to the expansion of  current partnerships and the 
development of  new ones.
5.    I am not unmindful of  the fact that given the global downturn 
of  the economy , corporate entities' commitment to the CSR 
sector is also adversely affected. This is one of  the reasons the 
NYSC Management is actively promoting the prospects of  
establishing the NYSC Trust Fund by the Federal Government. 
Through the establishment of  such a Fund, NYSC will not only 
be self-sustaining but will also be in a position to team up with you 
in assuring the future of  all our graduate youth in 
entrepreneurship. Needless to emphasise that unemployment, 
poverty , youth restiveness and criminality will be drastically 
reduced.

God bless you and continue to strengthen your organizations.

4. One of  the major areas of  focus is data control at all levels. 
As you are all aware, data generated from the Corps Producing 
Institutions is the raw material processed for the Mobilization 
exercise. This record is supposed to be pure and undiluted, but for 
selfish motives of  some players along the production chain, we 
have continued to encounter challenges. Let me, however, assure 
the public that we are not letting down our guard as we have 
continued to evolve and enhance control measures, including 
those that are technology-driven. These efforts require the buy-in 
of  other relevant stakeholders, including Students Affairs 
Officers (SAOs). The Workshop theme: “ Enhancing the 
Credibility of  the Mobilization Process through 
Effective Data Control,” is, therefore, a call to action for the 
SAOs to be above board in the discharge of  their responsibility of  
handling data generated for NYSC from the Corps Producing 
Institutions.

be processed for Exemption.

3. Distinguished ladies and gentlemen, today's event is the 
culmination of  the Presidential directive issued in 2016, which 
arose as a result of  the unfortunate deaths of  three Corps 
Members deployed to Kano, Zamfara and Bayelsa States' 
Orientation Camps. The loss of  any Corps Member as it were, 
provokes sadness in us, leaving the Scheme highly diminished. 
Corps Members, who represent the most critical part of  our 
demography – the youths, are the leaders and builders of  
tomorrow. Consequently , any Government policy aimed at 
uplifting this group is akin to building the future of  our dear 
country , Nigeria. It is particularly fulfilling that the enrolment of  
Corps Members into the Health Insurance Scheme is in line with 
the policy thrust of  my Administration bordering on the 
improvement of  welfare and security of  Corps Members and 
Staff.
4. This health initiative, known as NYSC Group Individual 
Family Social Health Insurance Programme, (GIFSHIP) has 
been designed as a holistic health insurance scheme, covering the 
periods of  Pre-Orientation, that is, as soon as a Prospective Corps 
Member picks up Call-up Letter, which is the instrument that 
qualifies him/her for admittance into National Service, until the 
end of  his/her terminal leave, which is three weeks after 
disengagement from Service.
worked assiduously and in concert with the NYSC in order to 
actualize Mr. President's directive to enroll Corps Members in the 
Insurance Scheme.

Maintenance Organizations (HMOs) have been carefully 
selected after a competitive process for each of  the six geopolitical 
zones to drive the process. To ensure seamless arrangement

failure. We will ensure that the operations of  the health scheme 
are consistent with the philosophy behind the initiation of  this 
wonderful health insurance scheme by Government.

INTRODUCTION
he dynamic nexus between military history and strategic 
Tleadership in any nation cannot be overemphasized. 
Indeed, an in-depth knowledge of  the former deepens 
and enhances the latter. Military history is a branch of  historical 
writing that systematically studies a nation's military activities and 
technology in the past, and the changes that had occurred over a 
period of  time. Such military activities include warfare, 
campaigns, tactics and strategies, effects of  warfare on the society , 
military-civil relations, among others. Of  significant importance 
in military history is the lesson that accompanies military 
activities, which is useful to the warriors, commanders/leaders or 
the society in general.  For instance, the lesson learnt from the 
battlefields by the surviving commanders and troops alike would 
help them not to repeat past mistakes but rather improve their 
tactics and techniques in subsequent battles.
MILIT ARY HISTORY AND THE RELEV ANCE OF 
STRA TEGIC LEADERSHIP: CHALLENGES AND 
PROSPECTS 
A PAPER PRESENTED TO THE COURSE 30 OF THE 
NA TIONAL DEFENCE COLLEGE, ABUJA, BY MAJOR 
GENERAL S IBRAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN 
FNARC MTRCN, DIRECTOR-GENERAL 
NA TIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS, 
ON FEBRUARY 21, 2022 
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
355
2.    In Africa, as it is in other parts of  the world, over the 
centuries, military warfare has led to the formation of  many 
empires, kingdoms and states. In fact, warfare has led to 
emergence of  warlords, energetic and visionary leaders, who 
administered their territories using military might before the 1
incursion of  European imperialists.  Thus, like Genghis Khan of  
the Mongolian empire, Napoleon Bonaparte of  monarchical 
France; Mao Tse Tung of  Communist China; Africa has had its 
own fair share of  warriors and military leaders in personalities 
such as Sundiata Somanguru of  ancient Mali empire, Askia the 
Great of  Songhai empire, Shaka of  the Zulu kingdom, Queen 
Amina of  Zauzau who deployed military experiences in 
developing their societies by engaging in wars.  Emphasizing this 
critical point, Shaibu while quoting Ukpabi avers that, “Nations 2
have been destroyed or built up and expanded through war”  The 
process of  warfare which culminated in the emergence of  leaders, 
states formation and expansion, and their subsequent collapse 
forms part of  military history , in which lesson could be learnt - not 
only by the leaders but the society at large.
3. Strategic leadership is the ability of  a leader to influence 
the people in order to accomplish the set goals of  the organization 
or the society . To successfully achieve this, Chemers maintains 
that the leader must have possessed certain qualities such as good 3
character, courage, prudence, and discipline,  among others. 
Thus, the linkage between military history and strategic

4. Paradoxically , many leaders have neglected the relevance 
of  military history in governance as lessons from the past are 
either ignored, neglected or have been simply and carelessly 
thrown to the dustbin. The overall consequence of  such careless 
actions is that society is set adrift, rudderless are in perpetual 
confusion. It is for this same reason too that Marcus Garvey , a 
foremost Pan Africanist, says a people without a knowledge of  5
their past history , origin and culture is like trees without roots.   In 
contemporary world, many nations are characterized majorly 
with absence of  good governance; this has resulted largely into 
insecurity in which the military has assumed an important role as 
peacekeepers, peace enforcers and peace builders. The quest for 
strategic leadership becomes imperative to overcoming the 
aforementioned challenges that threatened and has continued to 
threaten the existence of  mankind globally . The study of  military 
history by modern military professionals is critical to the 
development of  skills directly applicable on the battlefields of  
today and the future and in the management of  human society . It 
is in this context that this paper seeks to interrogate military 
history and its relevance to strategic leadership.  
leadership is in the lesson of  the past; for, according to Gbor, 
military history is an indispensable tool that anchors past military 
operations, institutional development and activities to the 4
present.   For this reason and many more, military history is one 
of  the veritable tools for developing the strategic thinking of  any 
leader because it provides a deep understanding of  the dynamic 
intersections -between war and society. This historical 
understanding would help the leaders and the society not to 
repeat the mistakes of  the past.

7. What is the Military? The wider usage of  the terms 
'military' and 'leadership' require conceptualization of  these two 
terms. This has become imperative so as to provide a contextual 
understanding in the usage of  the terms within the study . The 
usage of  'military' in public domain could be referred to as an 
organization which comprise the army , the navy and the air force, 
saddled with the responsibility of  maintaining the territorial 6
integrity of  a nation.   They engage in war, deter belligerent and 
also assist the police in internal security . In Nigeria, the military is 
also called armed forces; the two are sometimes used 
interchangeably .  Ekoko sees the military as the soldiers, army or

Clearly , a cursory look of  most armed forces globally seem to be

9. That said, what then is leadership? The subject of  
leadership has provoked a plethora of  publications, research and 
debate as a result of  which it is a key issue in scholarly discourse. 
Researchers have given meaning to the term in accordance with 
their disciplinary specializations. R.M, Stogdill cited in Tangban 
and  Audu defined leadership as the process or act of  influencing 
the activities of  an organised group in its efforts towards goal 10
setting and goal achievement.  Tangban and Audu also cited 
Bryman, who notes that a leader either in an organization or 
nation has a unique role in steering members of  that organization 
or nation towards a specified goal achievement of  enhanced 
performance in terms of  increased profitability or development 11
for an improved standard of  living.
10. M.P . Ntagu and L.O. Onuorah  however, holds the view 
that leadership is a body of  people who lead and direct the 
activities of  a group towards a shared goal. Leadership also 12
denote the ability to lead, direct and organise a group.  Similarly , 
Ntagu and Onuoha citing Gardner provide further explanation 
when they defined leadership as the process of  persuasion by 
which an individual induces a group to pursue objectives held by

the leader or shared by the leader and his or her followers.  
According to Chemers, leadership is a process of  social influence 
by which a person influences others to accomplish an objective 
and directs the organization in a way that makes it more cohesive 
and coherent. To him, a leader is expected to demonstrate 
qualities which embrace but not limited to good character, vision, 14
tact, courage and prudence.
11. In the context of  this perspectives, military is here defined 
as an institution trained in the art of  war. It comprises of  the army , 
the navy and the air force; while leadership means the ability of  a 
leader to influence the people or organised group in order to 
accomplish set goals of  an organisation or society . There is 
therefore a very important link between the military and strategic 
leadership which is required in every society for socio-economic 
and political development. The link is benchmarked by the fact 
that leadership could be a product of  sustained training which the 
military profession is better placed to give an individual and 
society . The emphasis on training here is deliberately anchored 
on the notion of  leadership which postulates that leaders are 15
made, they are never created.  The leader emerges from a social 
process or context to which he responds and in which he is 
relevant. To be a leader and remain relevant, leadership 
education, capacity building and leadership skills acquisition is 
imperative. I believe and am convinced; this is the purpose of  our

PERSPECTIVES ON MILITARY HISTORY AS A 
FIELD OF STUDY IN NIGERIA
being here today . We are here to learn skills, build our capacity in 
order to be better leaders in the society .    
12. Military history is an integral part of  history like all the 
other branches of  History . History may be defined as the corpus 
of  knowledge about the man's past, which comprises of  verified 
facts through honest inquiry , inferences, interpretations and 
generalizations by the Historian, and is available in the form of  16
records on paper or in memory .   Military history is therefore the 
body of  knowledge regardingarmed conflicts in the history of  17
humanity .  It initially focused on war:  how man and society used 
armed conflict to achieve political, social and economic goals. It 
narrates stories of  warfare in its entirety: the basis, nature, 
character and consequences of  warfare. Military history also 
provides critical insights on the dynamics of  war: what is 
changing, what has changed, and what has refused to change and 
why .
13. Some historians have observed that military history is 
better understood and appreciated within a time frame (see Table 18
1 above).  This is important to track changes and continuities, 
benchmark transitions and gage the implications of  these for 
human societies. Prior to the First World War, the subject matter 
of  military history was merely to narrate the conduct of  wars. It 
also focused on the description of  the processes and various stages in 
battles: who won, how and why; who lost, how and why? This

 TABLE1: THE PERIODIZAION OF MILITARY HISTORY 
AND CORRESPONDING CHANGES IN THE 
TECHNOLOGY OF WARFARE
PERIODS NOTABLE CHANGES
(a) Early to late Ancient 
Period (Classical Antiquity) 
(i) Man the hunter and gatherer
designed stones and shaped woods as 
weapons of  warfare.
(ii) The battle was initially against 
nature, and focused on the task of  
subduing the nature for survival 
(iii) When wars began to be fought in 
the late ancient period, weapons were 
sturdy and deploying them was 
clumsy , making mobility quite 
tasking.
(iv) Wars lasted for a very long time, 
sometimes for decades.
 
(v) Militaries were organized 
mainly to fight wars because 
Kingdoms  and empires survived 
on continues war. 
 
 
(b) The Medieval Period, 4th -
15th Century 
 
(i) Stirrups were invented and this 
changed the character of  warfare from 
antiquity .
 
(ii) Military tactics moved from  
massed infantry to Calvary-based 
forces and artillery , making war more 
dynamic  and decisive.
 
(iii) The notion of  a “standing 
army”
 
gained currency .

introduced.

that occurred (i. e. the consequences or impact).  Human 
condition thereafter became integral to the subject matter of  
military history. The focus of  military history thereafter 
expanded to include the consequences of  war on combatants and 
non-combatants; that is, war experiences and how wars 
happened the way they did. 
14. In Nigeria, the study of  military history evolved in the 
post-colonial period. It was S.C. Ukpabi that pioneered and 
professionalised the study of  military history in Nigeria. He th
traced Nigeria military history to the mid-19  Century when the 20
colonial army was formed.  Since then, it has only gained wider 
acceptability as a field of  study in the military institution and 
academics, though yet to be recognised at the conventional 
university system. Among the eminent scholars who have made 
useful contributions to the development of  military history in

Of  very important are the broad dimensions the works of

16.      According to C. N. Ubah, military history is a distinct 
subfield of  history capable of  responding to societal military 23
requirements.  He argues further that military history is the war 
15.  Ukpabi sees military history as a branch of  history that 
deal with warfare but not in isolation with the society . In many of  
his works, he holds the view that war was a central factor in 
human activities for thousands of  years. According to him, the 
branch of  study known as military history is that which explores 
how man has used armed conflict to accomplish “his political, 21
economic and societal goal.  He also dwells on the colonial 
formation of  the military particularly the Nigerian army and 
their major campaigns. He contends that the Nigerian army 
served the interests of  the colonialists as an instrument of  
coercion used to suppress many Nigerian societies. In one of  his 
works, he argued that poor organization of  the colonial army was 
majorly responsible for military's bad image up to the period of  22
independence.  Ukpabi as the pioneer Nigerian scholar in the 
field of  military history laid the foundation as most of  his works 
challenged Eurocentric views up to the period of  the Nigerian 
civil war.

dimension of  society's experience' and war is an aspect of  
society's relations with other societies. Ubah share similar view 
with S.C. Ukpabi, when he stated that war arises because of  the 
changing relations of  numerous variables-economic, social, 24
cultural, technological etc.
 17. From that view point, military history is the 
comprehensive understanding of  the relations between armed 
forces and society upon which war history rests. Ubah is of  the 
opinion that truly satisfactory military history should go beyond 
the narration and explanation of  episodic violence. He dwell on 
aspect of  asymmetry warfare, technology determinism in warfare 25
and the interaction of  war with the society .  Like Keegan in the 
Face of  Battle , Ubah believed that military history should be 
studied in width, depth and context. To study in width means to 
observe events comparatively over a long period of  time in order 
to observe change. To study in depth involves wide reading of  
sources to deduce real experiences and avoid any generalisation. 
Context involves treating the subject as a reflection of  social 
forces and not autonomously . Ubah contends that military history 
should not be saddled with the responsibility of  only studying the 
use of  armed forces during war time, but also in 'peacetime' or 
non-war periods.
18.     Ubah submits that military history should not be isolated 
from, but rather linked to, its parent discipline-history . The 
discipline of  history emphasizes objective analysis and critical 
thinking, rigorous research skills, an understanding of  the

 19. Gbor describes military history as an indispensable tool 
that anchors past military operations, institutional development 27
and activities to the present.  To him, the connection with the 
facts of  the past enables Generals and government officials to 
make informed decisions on military and defence matters. The 
factual understanding of  the past leads to the formulation of  the 
principle of  war, military tactics, military and defence policy , and 
above all, the development of  military strategy and doctrine.  
Military history , according to him, was inevitable for several 
reasons. Among which include new approach to military by 
academic military historians, changing nature of  war due to 28
modern technology ,  just to mention a few areas.

centres on modern military warfare, strategy and tactics.  His 
thought was greatly influenced by the new dimension to fighting 
terrorism and insurgency . To him, terrorism, insurgency and 
guerrilla warfare are the popular nomenclature used by non-state

23. There is no gainsaying that the study of  military history is 
very significant in the quest for strategic leadership. It has been 
firmly established that military history is not only the narration of  
war and biography or memoir of  the commanders, but the study 
of  human activities (social, economic and political) that 
culminated to war. There is a profound sense in which military 
history and strategic leadership coalesce. Strategic leadership  
embodies at least six elements, including but not limited to: (i) 
determining an organization's purpose and vision (ii) exploiting 
or maintaining core competencies; (iii) developing human capital; 
(iv) sustaining an effective  and result-oriented organizational 
culture; (v) Evolving and emphasizing ethical practices; and (vi) 
establishing a network of  balanced organizational controls, 33
including ensuring teamwork.  A very close look at these 
elements would reveal how they relate underscoring the 
importance for military history to strategic leadership in Nigeria. 
MILITARY HISTORY AND ITS RELEVANCE TO 
STRATEGIC LEADERSHIP
24. In the first place, military history does not only provide a 
blueprint or a roadmap, but it also provides a context that helps 
equip leaders to make informed decisions.  For instance, military 
history's utility value extends to matters of  policy and strategy . 
Knowledge of  a people's military past enhances adequate 
strategic choices by the policy makers. 
33
See O. O. Okpeh, "Strategic Leadership  and the Development Ques on", unpublished lecture 
delivered at a workshop organized for senior technocrats in Abuja by the Centre for Leadership 
in Nigeria, 2018

27. In addition, military history has often served as 
stimulators for technological improvements particularly in 
weapons, tactics and strategies. During the Nigerian Civil War, 
there was indigenous efforts at self-sustenance and self-defence by 
the South Easterner when they manufactured  Ogbunigwe . 
Ogbunigwe was a Biafran bomb produced to massively destroy 35
the enemy while fighting for self-preservation.  Successive 
generations can improve on it. 
25. Secondly , military history is a human preservation recipe. 
It informs its beneficiaries about dangers of  particular wars and 
benefits of  others through reflecting over the past. Similarly , it 
offers clues on prospects of  military advancement and or 
dynamics in technological attainments on which rests the decision 
on whether to embark on a particular war or desist. This is related 
to the role of  military history in giving impetus for specific wars or 
serving as deterrent to others.
26. Thirdly , military history is a veritable instrument of  
peaceful coexistence if  improperly handled or reconstructed. 
The gory images of  war in the past can make people to toe the line 
of  caution knowing fully well that the repercussion of  war is 
destruction. The gory images of  deaths in past wars can also be a 
cause of  war because it can serve as a stimulator for successive 
generations to engage in a retaliatory war. In the case of  the 
Nigerian Civil War, it has been argued that the quest for 
vengeance was partly the inciting factor for the formation of  the 34
Indigenous Peoples of  Biafra (IPOB) in South East Nigeria.

29. Military history probes the mentality and psychology of  
war captains and generals, thereby determining their impacts on 36
events.  The knowledge of  past battles helps leaders to 
understand their responsibilities. In particular, they will 
appreciate the importance of  discipline and the need to build 
confident and cohesive teams that are resilient to the debilitating 
effects of  combat trauma and the corrosive effects of  persistent 
danger.
30. Although there are clear practical applications of  the 
study of  war and warfare, such as understanding the 
fundamentals of  combined arms operations, the purpose of  
studying war through the lens of  history would be to make leaders 
wise forever.
28. Furthermore, military history in Nigeria has served the 
purposes of  national integration or nation building. Many 
military history scholars have reconstructed our national history 
to paint a heroic nationalistic image of  the nation's soldiers whose 
bravery and sacrifices have played major roles in our effort to 
remain a united nation particularly during the Nigeria Civil war 
and in the face ever-constant  and numerous ethno-religious 
conflicts. That is the major reason why the Nigerian government 
and the military celebrate the fallen heroes every year. Military 
history gives a sophisticated understanding of  the role of  the 
military and war in history . At other times, the military historian 
emphasizes or sometimes exaggerates the roles of  heroic soldiers 
of  the past. This may serve as a bonding force for the present and 
future generations.

S/N RELEVANCE/IMPORTANCE
q Military History is a great source of  applied 
knowledge required for strategic thinking. In this 
sense, it possesses a utilitarian value.
 
q
 
Military History is State history . The knowledge it 
makes one support nationalist cause and sentiments 
without which the nation ceases to exists . 
 
q
 
Through the study of  Military History officers are 
mentally equipped to face real/practical  life 
challenges.
 
q
 
Military History equips one with modern leadership 
skills required for solving practical organizational 
challenges and problems
 
q
 
For the military as an institution, a deep sense of  its  
emergence, growth and development (which should 
include challenges and achievements over time) is a 
great source of  institutional memory and heritage. 
q A careful study and understanding of  Military History 
educates us on the evolution of  technological 
advances in human societies through eras and ages.
q
 
Warfare exemplifies the collective actions of  a people. 
A deep sense of  this underscores the relevance of  team 
work,  planning, strategy and  execution in all human 
endeavor.

31. The unpopularity of  military history as a field of  study in 
the Nigerian conventional universities is one of  the challenges. 
The non-availability of  military history as a branch of  history in 
the conventional universities may partly be due to misconception 
of  the field to mean the study of  warfare and relic of  war alone, 
and partly because of  its newness in history . There are many 
branches of  history in the Nigerian conventional universities 
which include Economic, Social, Cultural, and Political History . 
Military History has only gained wider recognition in the military 
institutions and defence academies.  The study of  military history 
is imperative in the face of  the country's security challenges. To 
this end, courses that borders on military complex operation in 
war, military theory and doctrine, peacekeeping operation and 
peace building, counter- insurgency and counter-terrorism can 
be studied not only by the military personnel alone but others who 
may be interested.
32. Another challenge to military history is the limited 
numbers of  Military Historians. Only the Nigerian Defence 
Academy, Kaduna undertake military history courses and 
programmes both at degree and postgraduate levels. Though, 
some Military personnel and security experts have picked interest 
in the field, but that has not filled the huge gap of  scholars in the 
field, because they are not trained as professional military 
historian. In addition to this, there are dearth of  literature in 
military history .  
MILITARY HISTORY AND STRATEGIC 
LEADERSHIP: CHALLENGES AND PROSPECTS
33. In spite of  the challenges, there are a number of  prospects 
to military history and strategic leadership. In fact, for purposeful 
leadership, lessons of  history cannot be overemphasized. The 
knowledge of  military history particularly military relations

among various groups will assist in the building of  strong ties in 
the country .  
34. The knowledge of  military history will equip leaders to 
take informed decisions on matter of  defence and security . Also, 
understanding of  the societal ills through the lens of  military 
history would help leaders to avoid past mistakes. It is also 
important to state that there is continuous changing dynamics of  
armed conflict; knowledge of  the changing character of  warfare 
would no doubt spur the military to acquire advance military 
technology and be trained in intelligence gathering to solve 
mirage of  security problems. That will help the military to be 
offensive instead of  being defensive.

have stopped leading them". 
Colin Powell

it is not about organizations. it is 
not about plans. it is not about 
strategies. it is ab out people -

done. Y ou have to be people -
centered" Colin Powell

RECOMMENDATIONS
CONCLUSION
35. The paper examined the relevance of  military history to 
strategic leadership. Military as a distinct field of  history is the art 
and science of  historical reconstruction of  military activities as it 
affect the society . In Nigeria, it is an evolving field, taught in the 
military institution and academies but yet to take its roots in the 
conventional universities. Eminent scholars in the field have 
justified its importance and proved that it is beyond mere military 
affairs. No doubt, knowledge in the field of  military history is a 
veritable and indispensable tool to the leader, military personnel 
and policy makers particularly on matters that border on defence 
and security .  A well-researched military history will project the 
nation's image among the committee of  nations. The 
government and policy makers should strive hard to seeing that 
the study of  military history is not limited to military institutions 
and academies but should firmly be introduced in the nation's 
conventional universities. 
36. This paper therefore recommend the following as 
measures that should be considered to mainstreaming the study 
and application of  military history in our leadership and strategic 
thinking processes:
a. Prioritize the teaching of  History (and particularly 
Military History) in all military schools and research centers.
b. Deliberately evolving the culture of  documenting and 
properly keeping the records of  ALL military activities. 
c. Employ the services of  professional historians and bodies 
like the Historical Society of  Nigeria (established in 1953) to 
document the military as an institution
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
378
d. Establishment of  Military museums and archives to be 
manned by trained Military Historians and Archivists.
e. Generally creating more awareness on the relevance of  
Military History in the Military . 
f. According military research centers like the NDA Centre 
for Leadership and Complex Military Operations and the 
Nigerian Army Resource Center Abuja a central place in the 
training of  public officers.

Protocol
It is with immense delight that I welcome you on board as we 
formally induct you into the National Y outh Service Corps. I 
congratulate you on your graduation from your respective 
institutions of  learning, and your subsequent enlistment for the 
National Service. I also commend your patriotic zeal as 
demonstrated through acceptance of  your deployment and 
prompt report to this Orientation Camp.
2. My dear compatriots, the Orientation Course is the first 
Cardinal Programme of  NYSC, and is aimed at introducing you 
to the objectives and programmes of  the Scheme.   It is designed 
to equip you for the tasks of  the Service Y ear through lessons on 
the Cardinal Programmes, leadership coaching, paramilitary 
drills and other physical trainings as well as sensitization on 
topical national issues, amongst others. It is also a platform for 
kick-starting various activities that will enable you realize your 
potentials, and attain individual feats both within and beyond the 
period of  service. I, therefore, enjoin you to avail yourselves of  
this once-in-a-life-time opportunity by participating actively in all 
the Camp activities.

IN NIGERIA: THE NYSC IN PERSPECTIVE
A P APER DELIVERED BY THE DIRECTOR-GENERAL, 
NA TIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS, 
MAJOR GENERAL S IBRAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS 
FHSN FNARC M TRCN
A T THE GRAND RECEPTION/A W ARD CEREMONY

A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
4. There is a nexus that connects education and national 
development. Education remains the vehicle for effective national 
development in all nations, including Nigeria. Education, which 
is typically thought to have a big impact, is used to promote 
development. Education is the process of  enlightening people in 
their pursuits in life. Education and development are inextricably 
linked and interlinked. On the one hand, development aims to 
produce or create something new or more sophisticated for the 
benefit of  society and its members. Education, on the other hand, 
is a tool that can help people achieve their goals in life. And that is 
why Mr Barack Obama said that: 
3. Education is an important key to achieving sustainable 
national development. For a society to achieve a sustainable 
national development, the desire and process of  improving on its 
education must be a continuum. This brings to mind what former 
president of  the U.S, said about education. He said and I quote; 
“We have an obligation and a responsibility to be investing in our 
students and our schools. We must make sure that people who 
have the grades, the desire and the will, but not the money , can still 
get the best education possible” .
2. It is on this note that I reiterate the relevance of  education 
to national development in Nigeria which cannot be 
overemphasized. Since colonial era, education has been a top 
most priority even for colonial governments. Although, the type 
of  education that was given during this time was grossly 
inadequate as it was meant to meet the needs and demands of  
colonialism. Since independence in 1960, various governments 
have made efforts at developing and improving on our 
educational system.
386
A PUBLICATION OF THE NATIONAL YOUTH SERVICE CORPS 
NOT FOR SALE

SELECTED SPEECHES AND STRIDES OF THE 18TH NYSC DIRECTOR-GENERAL         
MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
6. However, for obvious reasons, education in Nigeria has 
been skewed towards white collar jobs. As you may be aware, 
these white collar jobs are shrinking by each passing day . It is 
against this background that I make the call to all relevant 
authorities to tailor our educational system towards self-reliance. 
Our students should be taught on how to be self-reliant and in the 
process, contribute to national development through the creation 
of  jobs, especially in the information technology sector. 
5. It can be deduced from the above therefore, that 
education and nation building are two inseparable variables that 
the former seems to directly determine whether the latter is going 
to be achieved or not and therefore, the need for a well-structured 
educational system that will enhance the achievement of  
development is required.
“In a global economy where the most valuable 
skill you can sell is your knowledge, a good 
education is no longer just a pathway to 
opportunity , it is a prerequisite… And when it 
comes to developing the high standards we 
need, it's time to stop working against our 
teachers and start working with them. Teachers 
don't go in to education to get rich. They don't 
go in to education because they don't believe in 
their children. They want their children to 
succeed, but we've got to give them the tools. 
Invest in early childhood education. Invest in 
our teachers and our children will succeed.”

10. The SAED programme if  expanded to continue after 
camp to enable the corps members, learn the various skills to 
certain level, and loans are granted to deserving corps members 
for investment in their business, the programme, no doubt will 
contribute more to national development especially in the area of  
job acquisition and youth self-dependency . The crisis of  white 
collar job and its attendant effect on the teeming Nigerian Y ouths 
7. It gives me joy to state categorically that we are already 
implementing this at the National Y outh Service Corps through a 
programme we call SAED. SAED is a skills acquisition and 
entrepreneurship development that aims at enhancing the 
economic mainstay of  corps members. This programme is 
deliberately designed that corps members are self-reliant after 
their service year. It is expected that through this programme, 
they will benefit and at the same time contribute to the economic 
development of  Nigeria. 
8. During the SAED programme, facilitators are engaged to 
train corps members in education, cosmetology , shoe making, 
beautification, culture and tourism, photography , food processing 
and preservation, power and energy , detergents making, ICT , 
solar and satellite installation, agro allied, hair making and 
barbing, design, tailoring, and so on in the in-camp training. 
9. Over the years since inception, the SAED programme 
has gone a long way in creating self-reliance and self-employment 
to thousands of  youths, especially the Nigeria youths who have 
been affected by the scourge of  unemployment overtime. It also 
helps to compliment the entrepreneurship courses that are 
introduced into Nigerian universities. It also guides them to know 
some of  the intricacies of  most Nigerian economic sectors as they 
are being required to be treated as staffs in their various places of  
primary assignment.

will be reduced to an extent as these youths are engaged in

11. Furthermore, a viable tool to this effect is the proposed

reliance and self-dependency . We have witnessed the nexus of  
education and national development lead to economic

China, India, Malaysia, Singapore that shaking off  the shackles 
of  underdevelopment by lifting their citizens out of  poverty and

reliance and self-dependency .

9.       Furthermore, I would like to reiterate our warning against 
unauthorized journeys and night trips. To greatly minimize the 
risk of  road traffic accident, you are expected to always cut short 
you trips from six o'clock in the evening and pass the night at 
military barracks and other locations officially designated as safe.  
Y ou are also strongly advised to avoid boarding vehicles at 
locations other than officially approved motor parks so as to avoid 
falling prey to criminals disguising as commercial vehicle drivers.
   
10.      Let me also use this opportunity to remind you of  the need 
to continue to observe the COVID-19 protocols wherever you 
find yourselves. For your information, the Federal Government's 
directive on the presentation of  evidence of  COVID-19 
vaccination as a pre-requisite for gaining entry to public offices 
subsists. Y ou are, therefore, advised to take the vaccine if  not done 
already . In addition, I charge you to help in sensitizing members 
of  the host communities about preventive measures, including 
the need to accept the vaccines.
11.    I consider it most appropriate to use this opportunity to once 
again express our profound gratitude to the Federal Government 
for providing the enablement for the take-off  of  Corps members' 
enrolment in the National Health Insurance Scheme under a 
comprehensive initiative known as NYSC Group Individual 
Family Social Health Insurance Programme (GIFSHIP). I enjoin 
all Corps members to take full advantage of  this arrangement by 
registering under Health Care Providers in their service locations, 
and always report promptly for medical attention in the event of  
ill health. Corps members can also visit any NHIS accredited 
hospital during official leave period outside their service 
locations.

2. As you are all aware, the evolution of  store management 
in the public service is to eliminate bottlenecks in the 
documentation of  official items, ensuring that goods and supplies 
keep to specified standards, as well as providing security for the 
goods. The nature of  operations of  the NYSC makes it necessary 
to adopt store management as a way of  ensuring risk reduction 
and timely dispatch of  goods such as Corps members' kit items 
and Orientation Course materials. The ever increasing Corps 
population also means that our supplies will keep rising even in 
the face of  limited spaces in our storage facilities.

4. Your Excellency, distinguished guests, ladies and 
gentlemen, the NYSC in almost forty-nine years has continued to 
provide successive batches of  Corps Members with the requisite 
platforms to make meaningful contributions to national 
development in various aspects of  our national life, such as unity 
and integration, education, health, infrastructure, participation 
in national elections, which has contributed towards conferring 
legitimacy on the electoral process as attested to by some 
governmental and non-governmental bodies, advocacies on 
social engineering and agriculture, amongst others. Against this 
backdrop, it is pertinent to state that the centrality of  the Corps to 
the national development agenda cannot be over-emphasized.
6. The philosophy behind the establishment of  these

5. The establishment of  NYSC Radio and Television is part

cause of  the Scheme, which today symbolizes national unity , and 
is in the forefront of  raising a crop of  youth entrepreneurs that 
contribute to the country's Gross Domestic Products through 
their exposure to the NYSC Skill Acquisition and 
Entrepreneurship Development training. While the NYSC 
Radio broadcasts on Channel 88.3 FM in Abuja, the NYSC 
Television runs on TStv Channel 365.

was to unveil his policy direction anchored on the 
following focal areas: 
iii. Improve on the welfare and security of  Corps members and Staff;

optimal benefits;

service delivery;

Entrepreneurship Development Programme (SAED) in line with the 
NYSC Act for greater impact. 
The Director-General immediately settled down for the day-to-
day running of  the Scheme with particular focus on his blueprint.

ii. SENSITIZATION OF THE PUBLIC ON THE 
NYSC ACT
The Director-General hosted a national sensitization programme 
on the NYSC Act in July 2019 and December 2021 in Abuja. 
Prior to this initiative, it was clear that many Nigerians were not 
aware of  the provisions of  the Act (a situation that had led to 
avoidable infractions). With the sensitization, which is still on-
going, organizations and individuals are now having better 
understanding of  their obligations to the Scheme. In particular, 
cases of  evasion and abscondment from Service, especially by 
foreign-trained Nigerian graduates, are expected to reduce 
drastically . 
f.   Major General Ibrahim also paid a visit to the composer of  the 
NYSC Anthem, seventy-four-year-old Dr. Oluwole Adetiran, at 
his home in Ogun State. He thanked him for bequeathing the 
Anthem as a legacy that has continued to inspire patriotism 
among Nigerian youths. It was the first of  such visit to him by any 
NYSC Director-General, and he expressed gratitude, saying he 
was fulfilled. As a follow-up action, the NYSC Management has 
further recommended Adetiran to Mr. President for the 
conferment of  National Honour.

MAJ G EN S IB RAHIM ASSOC. PROF . DSS FHSN MTRCN
Volume 3
Having uncovered the fraudulent activities of  some tertiary 
institutions in Africa, especially issuance of  Academic Certificates 
to unqualified persons, who in turn present same in an attempt to 
get mobilized for National Service, the Director-General 
commenced an aggressive fight against the menace.  In addition 
to hosting the maiden meeting of  the Scheme with Registrars of  
tertiary institutions from the affected countries in 2019 and 2021 
as part of  efforts to nip such sharp practices in the bud, internal 
mechanisms have been put in place for easier detection of  
unqualified persons attempting to present themselves for 
Mobilization.  As a result of  the stance of  the Management, some 
of  the foreign institutions are now volunteering to alert NYSC on 
suspected fraudulent practices by their students. Interestingly , out 
of  over twenty thousand (20,000) persons who registered online as 
foreign-trained Prospective Corps Members of  the 2019 Batch 
'C' Service Y ear, only three thousand four hundred and twenty 
(3,420) turned up for the Pre-Mobilization physical screening of  
credentials introduced by the Shuaibu-led Management. In order 
to serve as deterrent to others, sixty-five (65) fake Corps members 
arrested during the 2019 Batch 'B' Stream II Orientation Course 
in Camps across the country are being prosecuted with some 
convictions already secured. These steps taken by the 
Management have helped to create national awareness, especially 
on the need for parents and guardians to check the accreditation 
status of  institutions attended by their children and to monitor 
their academic progress. The bold move by the Director-General 
in sanitizing the Mobilization process will also ensure that only 
well-trained and competent persons occupy positions that will 
fast-track the future development of  the country . This has also led 
to the closure of  many fake institutions in some of  the affected 
countries.

For the first time in the history of  the NYSC, the Management 
under Major General S Ibrahim convened a meeting with 
Ministries, Departments and Agencies as well as Professional 
Bodies with operational link to the Scheme. The meeting evolved 
measures to promote the quality of  education, especially in 
relation to the attendance of  foreign tertiary institutions by 
Nigerian youth as well as address issues militating against the 
Mobilization process. It has further prompted the Federal 
Ministry of  Education to set up an inter-agency committee, with 
NYSC as a member, to check the activities of  fraudulent foreign 
institutions and their collaborators.

vii. REINVIGORATION OF THE NYSC VENTURES
In pursuit of  one of  the Director-General's Agenda, 
Management is reinvigorating the various NYSC V entures with 
the following feats achieved so far:
· The NYSC Water Factory and the NYSC Bakery both 
located at the Permanent Orientation Camp, Kubwa, 
FCT , are fully back on stream with their products being 
patronized by the public. 
· The Scheme is revamping the NYSC Garment Factories 
located in Minna, Niger State and Mgbaku, Anambra 
State. 
· The operations of  the NYSC Farm Settlements across the 
country are being enhanced, especially with supply of  
equipment and other necessary inputs to the farms 
located in the FCT as well as Bauchi, Kebbi and Oyo 
States.
· As a result of  sustained advocacy by the Director-
General, the Scheme has been given back the NYSC 
farmland at Ezillo, which was hitherto taken by the 
Ebonyi State Government. 
· Procurement of  tractor for farming operations at the 
NYSC farm Ezillo, Ebonyi State.
· Initiation of  partnerships with the National Agricultural 
Land Development Agency (NALDA), International 
Institute of  Tropical Agriculture (IITA), Agricultural and 
Rural Management Training Institute (ARMTI), the 
National Centre for Agricultural Mechanization 
(NCAM) and the National Cereals Research Institute 
(NCRI) on the training of  Corps members and Staff  as 
well as deployment of  modern farming techniques and 
equipment.
· Resuscitation of  the moribund NYSC Feed Mill, Lagos,

viii.   REGISTRATION OF NYSC VENTURES WITH

In a bid to give impetus to the revenue generation drive of  the

Corporate Affairs Commission. They are the NYSC Garment

Mill, Ipaja, Lagos State as well as the NYSC Entertainment 
Company Limited, which comprises the NYSC National Band, 
NYSC National Cultural Troupe and the NYSC Movie 
(NYSCwood).

x. INSCRIPTION OF DATE OF BIRTH ON THE 
CERTIFICATE OF NATIONAL SERVICE 
In a bid to check manipulation of  date of  birth by ineligible 
persons seeking mobilization for National Service, the present 
Management decided to inscribe date of  birth on the Certificate 
of  National Service beginning with the 2019 Batch 'A' Corps 
members. The inscription of  the date of  birth on Exclusion 
Letters also commenced from the 2019 Batch 'C' Service Y ear.  
unprecedented achievement has been hailed by the higher 
authorities, including the National Assembly .
